Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Pillars of Salah: Qiyam, Qira'ah, Ruku', Sujud
Definition and scriptural evidence for the four pillars of salah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four pillars of salah in the Hanafi school, identify the Quranic evidence for each, and explain the minimal requirement for ruku' and sujud.

Core Idea
The four pillars of salah are standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration; omitting any invalidates the prayer.

This lesson focuses on the essential pillars (arkan) of the prayer according to the Hanafi school. The passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah provides the definition and proof for each pillar, emphasizing that the minimal act qualifies. Understanding these pillars is fundamental because their omission completely invalidates the salah, unlike the wajibat which require compensation. We will also examine an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on sujud and the cross-madhhab difference with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four pillars
List the four acts that the passage explicitly states as pillars: qiyam (standing), qira'ah (recitation), ruku' (bowing), and sujud (prostration with forehead and nose).
These are the only arkan according to the Hanafi school; other acts like i'tidal and jalsah are wajib or sunnah.
2
Locate the Quranic evidence
For each pillar, find the verse cited. Qiyam: al-Baqarah 2:238; Qira'ah: al-Muzzammil 73:20; Ruku' and Sujud: al-Hajj 22:77. Note the imperative form indicating obligation.
The word 'qanitin' in the qiyam verse has multiple interpretations, but the command to stand is clear.
3
Analyze the minimal requirement
The passage states that the rukn (pillar) is the minimum act to which the name applies. For ruku', any bending that qualifies as bowing; for sujud, touching the forehead and nose to the ground.
Anything beyond the minimum (e.g., extra bending, prolonged prostration) is either wajib or mustahabb.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on sujud
Early Hanafis differed: some allowed sujud with only the nose. The passage states 'bi akhadh a' indicating later scholars (mutakhkhirin) adopted requiring both forehead and nose, and this is the mufta bihi.
The phrase 'wa bihi akhadh' signals the operative fatwa.
5
Consider cross-madhhab differences
The Shafi'i school includes additional acts like the final sitting (jalsah akhir) and tashahhud as pillars. For Hanafis, these are wajib. This affects whether omission invalidates the prayer or requires sajdah al-sahw.
Such differences are legitimate ikhtilaf and reflect different usul approaches.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة صفة الصلاة والقيام، والقراءة، والركوع، والسجود بالجبهة والأنف، وبه أخذ. [٢]قوله : والقيام ؛ لقوله : ( وَقُومُوا لِلَّهِ قَنِتِينَ ) ، أي داعين أو خاشعين متواضعين، أو ساكتين على اختلاف الأقوال وأظهرها آخرها. [٣] قوله : والقراءة ؛ أي مطلقها من غير تعيين الفاتحة وغيرها ؛ لقوله : فَاقْرَءُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنْهُ [٤] قوله : والركوع والسجود ؛ لقوله : يَتَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا أَرْكَعُوا واسْجُدُوا ) ، والركن منهما أدنى ما يطلق عليه اسم الركوع والسجود، وما زاد عليه واجب أو مستحب. [0]قوله : وبه أخذ ؛ بصيغة المجهول، أي أخذ به المشايخ وأفتوا به
The Book of Prayer: Description of the prayer: Standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration with the forehead and nose, and with this they took. [2] He said: 'Standing'; due to His statement: 'And stand before Allah in devout obedience' (al-Baqarah 2:238), meaning supplicating or humbly submissive, or silent, according to different opinions and the most apparent is the last. [3] He said: 'Recitation'; i.e., absolutely without specifying Fatiha or otherwise; due to His statement: 'So recite what is easy of it' (al-Muzzammil 73:20). [4] He said: 'Bow and prostrate'; due to His statement: 'O you who believe, bow and prostrate' (al-Hajj 22:77). And the pillar (rukn) of each is the minimum to which the name of bowing and prostration applies, and what is additional is obligatory or recommended. [0] He said: 'And with this they took'; in the passive voice, i.e., the scholars took it and gave fatwa accordingly.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage delineates the pillars (arkan) of the salah according to the Hanafi school. There are four: standing (qiyam), recitation (qira'ah), bowing (ruku'), and prostration (sujud) with both the forehead and nose. The evidence for standing is the Quranic command in Surah al-Baqarah 2:238, which is interpreted as standing in devotion. For recitation, the evidence is the general command in Surah al-Muzzammil 73:20 to recite whatever is easy, indicating no specific surah is mandated for the fard, though the Fatiha is wajib. For bowing and prostration, the evidence is the command in Surah al-Hajj 22:77. The commentary explains that the rukn (pillar) of each is the minimal act to which the name applies—any movement that qualifies as bowing or prostration fulfills the pillar, and anything beyond that is either wajib or mustahabb. The final statement 'bi akhadh a' indicates that the scholars, particularly the later ones (mutakhkhirin), adopted the position that sujud must be performed with both the forehead and nose, and they gave fatwa upon that, not allowing the nose alone without excuse.

Key Terms
قيام (qiyām): Standing upright during the prayer; a pillar that must be performed if physically able.
قراءة (qirā'ah): Recitation of Quran in the prayer; any verse suffices for the fard, though Fatiha is wajib.
ركوع (rukū'): Bowing so that the hands can reach the knees; minimal degree is sufficient for the pillar.
سجود (sujūd): Prostration with forehead and nose on the ground; both are required per the operative fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a pillar (rukn) of salah according to this passage?
A) Qiyam
B) Qira'ah
C) Raf' al-Yadayn
D) Ruku'

Key Takeaway
The four pillars of salah—standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration with forehead and nose—are established by Quranic commands, and their omission invalidates the prayer; the minimal act suffices for the pillar, and later Hanafi scholars affirmed sujud requires both forehead and nose.

Salah — Prayer

The Fard Acts of Prayer and the Dispute on Takbir Tahrimah
Listing obligatory acts of prayer and defending Hanafi view on takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five fard acts of prayer according to the Hanafi school and explain the Hanafi rebuttal to the Shafi'i claim that the opening takbir is a rukn.

Core Idea
The opening takbir is fard, not rukn — the hadith cited is not literal, otherwise tasbih would also be a pillar.

In this passage, the commentator on Al-Wiqayah outlines the fundamental obligatory (fard) acts of prayer and immediately enters a classical dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the legal nature of the opening takbir (takbir tahrimah). The Hanafi school holds that the takbir is a fard obligation, not an integral pillar (rukn), and the Shafi'i counter-argument is met with a sophisticated textual analysis. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly assessing the validity of a prayer when the takbir is omitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five fard acts of prayer
From the passage, list the five acts designated as fard: takbir tahrimah (opening takbir), qiyam (standing), qira'ah (recitation), ruku' (bowing), and sujud (prostration).
Note the specific condition for sujud: it must involve both the forehead and nose.
2
Understand the dispute on takbir
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i considers the opening takbir a rukn (integral pillar) based on the hadith: 'إنما هي التكبير والتسبيح وقراءة القرآن'. The Hanafi response is that this hadith is not taken literally (متروك الظاهر).
If taken literally, tasbih (glorification) would also be a rukn, which is false by consensus.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response in detail
The Hanafi argument: (a) the hadith is abandoned in its apparent meaning; (b) the word 'تكبير' may refer to the takbirs of transitions, not specifically the opening takbir; (c) there is no explicit evidence that the opening takbir is a part (جزء) of prayer.
This shows the Hanafi principle of not taking a general statement as definitive without considering context and consensus.
4
Examine the Quranic proofs for the other acts
Each fard act is supported by a Quranic verse: standing (2:238: 'وَقُومُوا لِلَّهِ قَنِتِينَ'), recitation (73:20: 'فَاقْرَءُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنْهُ'), bowing and prostration (22:77: 'ارْكَعُوا وَاسْجُدُوا').
These are treated as direct dalil for obligation, but the definition of the rukn for bowing and prostration is minimal.
5
Distinguish fard vs. rukn in Hanafi usul
In the Hanafi school, a fard is an obligatory act established by definitive evidence; a rukn is an integral part of the prayer. Here, the five acts are called fard, not rukn, except that the minimal bending in ruku' and sujud is considered the rukn of those acts.
The practical consequence (thamarah) is that omission of a fard (like takbir) does not automatically invalidate the prayer if it is unintentional, whereas omission of a rukn does.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة صفة الصلاة
والقيام، والقراءة، والركوع، والسجود بالجبهة والأنف، وبه أخذ
وعند الشافعي ركن، فأما رفع اليدين فسنة.
والأصل في العطف المغايرة، فعلم منه أن التحريمة مغايرة للصلاة، وهي تعقبها وتتصل بها.
قوله: ركن؛ لقوله عليه السلام: «إن هذه الصلاة لا يصلح فيها شيء من كلام الناس إنما هي التكبير والتسبيح وقراءة القرآن»، ونحن نقول: إنه متروك الظاهر، وإلا يلزم كون التسبيح ركنا، وليس كذلك بالإجماع، وأيضا لا دلالة على جزئية تكبيرة التحريمة؛ لاحتمال أن يكون المراد به تكبيرات الانتقالات.
قوله: والقيام؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَقُومُوا لِلَّهِ قَنِتِينَ﴾، أي داعين أو خاشعين متواضعين، أو ساكتين على اختلاف الأقوال وأظهرها آخرها.
قوله: والقراءة؛ أي مطلقها من غير تعيين الفاتحة وغيرها؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاقْرَءُوا مَا تَيَسَّرَ مِنْهُ﴾.
قوله: والركوع والسجود؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا ارْكَعُوا وَاسْجُدُوا﴾، والركن منهما أدنى ما يطلق عليه اسم الركوع والسجود، وما زاد عليه واجب أو مستحب.
Book of Prayer: Description of Prayer. Standing, recitation, bowing, and prostration with the forehead and nose, and this is what was adopted. According to al-Shafi'i, it is a pillar (rukn), but raising the hands is sunnah. The principle in conjunction is difference, so it is known that the opening takbir is different from the prayer, and it follows it and is connected to it. His saying: 'A pillar' due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Indeed this prayer is not suitable for any speech of people; it is only takbir, tasbih, and recitation of the Quran.' And we say: It is abandoned in its apparent meaning, otherwise tasbih would be a pillar, but that is not the case by consensus. Also there is no evidence for the integral nature of the opening takbir because it is possible that what is meant is the takbirs of transitions. His saying: 'Standing' due to the Almighty's saying: 'And stand before Allah devoutly' meaning supplicating or humble or silent according to different opinions, the most apparent being the last. His saying: 'Recitation' meaning absolutely, without specifying al-Fatiha or others, due to the Almighty's saying: 'So recite what is easy from it.' His saying: 'Bowing and prostration' due to the Almighty's saying: 'O you who believe, bow and prostrate.' The integral (rukn) of them is the minimum that the name of bowing and prostration applies to, and what is more than that is obligatory or recommended.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah begins by stating the obligatory (fard) acts of prayer: standing (qiyam), recitation (qira'ah), bowing (ruku'), and prostration (sujud) with both forehead and nose. The author notes that the later scholars adopted this view. Then he addresses a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the opening takbir (takbir tahrimah). The author explains that in the matn, the conjunction indicates that the takbir is distinct from the prayer itself. He then critiques the Shafi'i proof that the takbir is a rukn (integral pillar) based on the hadith 'Prayer consists of takbir, tasbih, and Quran recitation.' The Hanafi response is that the hadith cannot be taken literally, otherwise tasbih would also be a rukn—which is not the case by consensus. Moreover, the word 'takbir' could refer to the takbirs during transitions, not specifically the opening takbir. Following this, the commentator provides Quranic proofs for standing (Quran 2:238), recitation (Quran 73:20), and bowing and prostration (Quran 22:77). For the latter, he clarifies that the minimal act that qualifies as ruku' or sujud is the integral, while additional movements are either obligatory or recommended. The overall emphasis is that these five acts are fard, not rukn, with the takbir dispute highlighting the Hanafi method of interpreting evidence.

Key Terms
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir (saying Allahu Akbar) that commences the prayer.
ركن (rukn): An integral part of an act of worship; its omission invalidates the act.
فرض (fard): An obligatory act established by definitive evidence (Quran or mutawatir hadith).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what category does the opening takbir (tahrimah) fall under?
A) Rukn (integral pillar)
B) Fard (obligatory)
C) Sunnah (recommended)
D) Mustahabb (preferred)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between fard and rukn; the takbir tahrimah is fard, not rukn, based on a contextual reading of the hadith and consensus that tasbih is not a pillar.

The Hanafi Intra-School Dispute on Sufficing with the Nose in Sujud
Intra-Hanafi dispute with hadith evidence and later school tarjih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on sufficing with the nose in sujud, explain the evidence for each, and identify the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The mufta bihi requires both forehead and nose in sujud, not just the nose alone.

When performing sujud, one of the seven limbs must be placed on the ground. The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement: does sufficing with only the nose count? Abu Hanifa allowed it based on the general meaning of 'face' in the hadith, but his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, required the forehead as well. This lesson examines the evidence and clarifies which position is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disagreement
What specific ruling is disputed? Is it valid to suffice with the nose alone in sujud without an excuse?
2
State the positions of each imam
Abu Hanifa permits sufficing with the nose; the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require both forehead and nose.
3
Analyze the evidence
How does each side argue from the hadith of the seven limbs? Abu Hanifa uses the general term 'face'; the Sahibayn emphasize the forehead as the primary part.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical consequence? According to Abu Hanifa, sujud with only the nose is valid but makruh; according to the Sahibayn, it invalidates the prayer.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi scholars (mashayikh) declared the fatwa is on the view of the Sahibayn; sujud with only the nose is not permissible.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجوز عند أبي حنيفة الاكتفاء بالأنف عند عدم العذر خلافاً لهما
لا يخلو عن مسامحة؛ لأن المفهوم من ظاهر قوله: والسجود بالجبهة والأنف عندنا تعداد الفرائض، أن وضع الجبهة والأنف كليهما فرض، وأنه المفتى به، مع أنه ليس مذهباً لأحد من أئمتنا.
فإن أبا حنيفة جوز الاكتفاء بالأنف، وخالفه فيه صاحباه.
وأما الاكتفاء بالجبهة فهو متفق بينهم على جوازه.
وبالجملة اتفقوا على أن المسنون هو وضع الجبهة والأنف كليهما، وعلى أنه يكفي وضع الجبهة فقط، إلا أنه يكره، وإنما اختلفوا في الاكتفاء بالأنف، وإن حمل قوله على أن وضع الجبهة أو الأنف فرض بأن تكون الواو بمعنى أو، ويكون الغرض منه بيان مذهب أبي حنيفة.
ورد عليه أنه ليس مفتى به عند مشايخنا، فقد صرح أصحاب الكتب المتداولة أن المفتى به هو قولهما، وهو رواية عنه أنه لا يجوز الاكتفاء بالأنف، والعجب من الشارح له حيث لم يتنبه على مسامحة المصنف، وقال في «مختصره» تبعاً له: والسجود بالجبهة والأنف وبه يفتى، مع تصريحه هاهنا بأن الفتوى على قولهما، وللناظرين هاهنا كلمات بيناها في «السعاية».
قوله: الاكتفاء بالأنف؛ لحديث: «إذا سجد العبد سجد معه سبعة آراب - أي أعضاء: وجهه، وكفاه، وركبتاه، وقدماه، فإن الوجه هاهنا مطلق، وجميع أجزائه ليس بمراد إجماعاً، فإن الاقتصار على الخدين والذقن لا يجوز اتفاقاً، فتعين أن يكون المراد به الجبهة والأنف؛ لكونهما محل السجود، فكما يجوز الاكتفاء بالجبهة يجوز الاكتفاء بالأنف.
According to Abu Hanifa, it is permissible to suffice with the nose when there is no excuse, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). This statement is not free from inaccuracy, because what is understood from the apparent meaning of his saying: 'And prostration with the forehead and the nose' is that among us it counts the obligations, that placing both the forehead and the nose is fard, and that this is the mufta bihi, even though it is not the school of any of our imams. For Abu Hanifa permitted sufficing with the nose, and his two companions disagreed with him. As for sufficing with the forehead, it is agreed among them that it is permissible. In summary, they agreed that the sunnah is to place both the forehead and the nose, and that placing only the forehead suffices but is disliked. They only differed on sufficing with the nose. And if his statement is interpreted to mean that placing the forehead or the nose is fard, taking the 'waw' to mean 'or', and the purpose is to state the school of Abu Hanifa, it is objected that this is not mufta bihi among our scholars. Indeed, the authors of the circulating books have explicitly stated that the mufta bihi is their (the two companions') view, and there is a narration from him (Abu Hanifa) that sufficing with the nose is not permissible. It is surprising that the commentator (al-Sharh) did not notice the inaccuracy of the author (al-Wiqayah), and said in his 'Mukhtasar' following him: 'And prostration with the forehead and the nose, and this is the fatwa,' while he states here that the fatwa is on their view. And for the observers there are words we have explained in 'al-Si'aya'. His saying: 'Sufficing with the nose' due to the hadith: 'When the slave prostrates, he prostrates with seven limbs: his face, his palms, his knees, and his feet.' The 'face' here is general, and all its parts are not intended by consensus, for limiting it to the cheeks and chin is not permissible by agreement. So it is determined that what is meant is the forehead and the nose, for they are the place of prostration. Just as sufficing with the forehead is permissible, so too is sufficing with the nose permissible.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding sujud. The matn of Al-Wiqayah states that prostration is with the forehead and nose, and 'this is what was adopted.' The commentator (Sharh al-Wiqayah) notes that this phrasing is imprecise. The apparent meaning suggests that both forehead and nose are obligatory (fard) and that this is the mufta bihi (relied-upon position for fatwa). However, this is not the school of any of the Hanafi imams. In reality, Abu Hanifa allowed sufficing with the nose when there is no excuse, but the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) required both forehead and nose. They agree that sufficing with just the forehead is permissible (though disliked), and that the sunnah is to place both. The only disagreement is about sufficing with the nose. The commentator then explains that if one interprets the matn's 'waw' as 'or' to indicate that either the forehead or the nose suffices, that would reflect Abu Hanifa's view. But this is not the mufta bihi; the later scholars (mashayikh) have declared that the fatwa is on the view of the Sahibayn, and there is even a narration from Abu Hanifa prohibiting sufficing with the nose. The commentator criticizes the author of the Sharh for not noticing this inaccuracy and for contradicting himself. Finally, a hadith is cited to support Abu Hanifa's original view: the Prophet said that the seven limbs of prostration include the face, which encompasses both forehead and nose. Since the face is general, and consensus excludes the cheeks and chin, the intended meaning is the forehead and nose. If the forehead is sufficient, then by analogy the nose should also be sufficient, as both are part of the face. However, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that both are required, and sujud with only the nose is invalid.

Key Terms
الأنف (al-anf): The nose; in sujud, it is a limb used for prostration.
الجبهة (al-jabha): The forehead; the primary part of the face for prostration.
مفتى به (mufta bihi): The ruling that is relied upon for issuing fatwas, i.e., the operative position in the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, what is required for sujud?
A) Only the forehead
B) Only the nose
C) Both forehead and nose
D) Either forehead or nose

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi requires both forehead and nose in sujud; sufficing with only the nose invalidates the prayer.

Sujood: Forehead vs. Nose and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sufficiency of nose for sujood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding sufficiency of the nose in sujood, and identify the mufta bihi (operative ruling) in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
In sujood, the forehead is required; the nose alone suffices only according to the non-operative view of Abu Hanifa.

This passage examines an internal Hanafi disagreement about whether placing only the nose during prostration is sufficient when there is no excuse. Abu Hanifa allowed it based on the hadith mentioning 'face,' which includes the nose. His two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, required the forehead, and their view became the fatwa. Understanding this dispute clarifies the school's methodology in weighing textual evidence and resolving ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ikhtilaf
The act is sujood (prostration) in salah. The point of disagreement is whether the nose alone suffices when there is no excuse, without the forehead touching.
The forehead alone is agreed to suffice, though disliked.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his dalil
Abu Hanifa holds that the nose alone is sufficient. His proof is the hadith mentioning 'face' among the seven limbs; since 'face' is absolute and includes the nose, the nose suffices.
Consensus excludes cheeks and chin, so the locus is forehead and nose.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their dalil
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad require the forehead. They argue that some narrations interpret 'face' as specifically the forehead, and the consistent practice of the Prophet was to place his forehead.
The Sahibayn also note the sunnah is to place both, but the minimum is the forehead.
4
Recognize the mufta bihi and tarjih
The fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view. Later Hanafi masters (authors of standard books) declared that the operative ruling is that the nose alone is insufficient; the forehead must touch.
This is despite some texts inconsistently stating the fatwa on Abu Hanifa's view.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجوز عند أبي حنيفة الاكتفاء بالأنف عند عدم العُذر خلافاً لهما لا يخلو عن مسامحة ؛ لأنّ المفهوم من ظاهر قوله : والسجود بالجبهة والأنف عندنا تعداد الفرائض، أنَّ وضع الجبهة والأنف كليهما فرض، وأنه المفتى به، مع أنه ليس مذهباً الأحد من أئمتنا. فإنَّ أبا حنيفة جوز الاكتفاء بالأنف، وخالفه فيه صاحباه. وأما الاكتفاء بالجبهة فهو متفق بينهم على جوازه. وبالجملة اتفقوا على أنَّ المسنون هو وضع الجبهة والأنف كليهما، وعلى أنه يكفي وضع الجبهة فقط، إلا أنه يكره، وإنّما اختلفوا في الاكتفاء بالأنف، وإن حمل قوله على أن وضع الجبهة أو الأنف فرض بأن تكون "الواو" بمعنى "أو"، ويكون الغرض منه بيان مذهب أبي حنيفة . ورد عليه أنه ليس مفتی به عند مشايخنا ، فقد صرح أصحاب الكتب المتداولة أنَّ المفتى بـه هـو قـولهما، وهو رواية عنه أنه لا يجوز الاكتفاء بالأنف، والعجب من الشارح له حيث لم يتنبه على مسامحة المصنف ، وقال في "مختصره" تبعاً له : والسجود بالجبهة والأنف وبه يفتى ) ، مع تصريحه هاهنا بأنَّ الفتوى على قولهما، وللناظرين هاهنا كلمات بيناها في "السعاية". [١] قوله : الاكتفاء بالأنف ؛ لحديث: "إذا سجد العبد سجد معه سبعة آراب - أي أعضاء : وجهه، وكفاه، وركبتاه، وقدماه ، فإنّ الوجه هاهنا مطلق ، وجميع أجزائه ليس بمراد إجماعاً، فإنّ الاقتصار على الخدين والذقن لا يجوز اتفاقاً، فتعين أن يكون المراد به الجبهة والأنف ؛ لكونهما محلّ السجود، فكما يجوز الاكتفاء بالجبهة يجوز الاكتفاء بالأنف. وجوابه : إنَّ الوجه في هذه الرواية التي رواها أصحاب السنن وغيرهم مفسّر بالجبهة كما ورد التصريح به في بعض روايات مسلم والنسائي.
It is permissible according to Abu Hanifa to suffice with the nose when there is no excuse, contrary to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). This is not free from imprecision, because what is understood from the apparent meaning of his statement: 'And prostration is with the forehead and the nose according to us' in the enumeration of obligations is that placing both the forehead and the nose is obligatory, and that is the fatwa, even though it is not the madhhab of any of our imams. Indeed, Abu Hanifa allowed sufficing with the nose, and his two companions differed with him. As for sufficing with the forehead, they all agreed on its permissibility. In summary, they agreed that the sunnah is to place both the forehead and the nose, and that it suffices to place only the forehead, but it is disliked. They only differed regarding sufficing with the nose. If his statement is interpreted that placing the forehead or the nose is obligatory, with the 'waw' meaning 'or', then the purpose would be to state the madhhab of Abu Hanifa. It was objected that this is not the operative fatwa according to our scholars, for the authors of the standard books have stated that the fatwa is his (i.e., their) statement, and it is a narration from him that sufficing with the nose is not permissible. It is surprising that the commentator (al-Sharh) did not notice the imprecision of the author (al-Musannif), and said in his 'Mukhtasar' following him: 'And prostration is with the forehead and the nose, and with it is the fatwa', while he states here that the fatwa is on their statement. The scholars here have words which we have explained in 'al-Si'ayah'. [The author says: 'His statement: sufficing with the nose is because of the hadith: "When the slave prostrates, he prostrates with seven limbs" – i.e., organs: his face, his two hands, his two knees, and his two feet. For the face here is absolute, and all its parts are not intended by consensus, because limiting to the two cheeks and the chin is not permissible by agreement. So it is determined that what is meant is the forehead and the nose, because they are the place of prostration. So just as sufficing with the forehead is permissible, sufficing with the nose is permissible.' The response: The face in this narration narrated by the authors of the Sunan and others is interpreted as the forehead, as explicitly stated in some narrations of Muslim and al-Nasa'i.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the sufficiency of the nose alone for prostration (sujood) in prayer. The author begins by stating that Abu Hanifa permits sufficing with the nose when there is no excuse, contrary to his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. He notes that the wording in some texts suggests both forehead and nose are obligatory, but that is not the actual school position. The agreed-upon sunnah is to place both, and sufficing with the forehead alone is permissible but disliked. The core disagreement concerns the nose alone. The text then cites a hadith about the seven limbs of prostration, arguing that the 'face' includes both forehead and nose, so either suffices. However, the response (from the Sahibayn's perspective) is that the hadith is interpreted as specifically the forehead in some authentic narrations. The fatwa is ultimately on the opinion of the two companions, meaning the nose alone is insufficient. The commentary expresses surprise that some authors inconsistently state the fatwa as on Abu Hanifa’s view while affirming the contrary.

Key Terms
الأنف (al-anf): The nose; one of the seven limbs of prostration.
الجبهة (al-jabhah): The forehead; the primary limb for sujood.
الوجه (al-wajh): The face; in the context of the hadith, interpreted as the forehead and nose.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (operative ruling) in the Hanafi school, what is required for a valid sujood?
A) Both forehead and nose must touch the ground
B) The forehead must touch the ground; the nose is sunnah
C) The nose alone is sufficient
D) Any part of the face suffices

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the operative ruling for sujood requires the forehead to touch the ground; the nose is sunnah and its omission is makruh but the prayer remains valid if the forehead is placed.

Salah — Prayer

Evidence for Obligation of Final Sitting
Proof from Quran and Sunnah that final sitting is fard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers the final sitting (al-qa'dah al-akhirah) an obligatory pillar (fard) of prayer, citing the Quranic evidence and the Prophet's consistent practice, and contrast it with the non-obligatory first sitting.

Core Idea
The final sitting in prayer is fard – the Quranic commands and the Prophet's unwavering practice establish its necessity.

The final sitting is the moment in prayer when the worshipper sits after the last prostration, reciting the tashahhud. While other schools regard it as a recommended act, the Hanafi school insists it is a fard (obligatory pillar). This lesson examines the textual and practical proofs marshalled by Hanafi scholars – from Quranic imperatives to the Prophet's consistent example – to demonstrate why the final sitting cannot be omitted without invalidating the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The final sitting (al-qa'dah al-akhirah) is the act under consideration. The Hanafi ruling is that it is fard (obligatory), forming a rukn of prayer.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence
The passage cites four verses containing imperative forms: 'Magnify your Lord' (al-Muddaththir:3), 'Stand devoutly' (al-Baqarah:238), 'Recite' (al-Muzzammil:20), and 'Bow and prostrate' (al-Hajj:77). In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is a contrary indicator. These commands are not fulfilled outside prayer, so they must refer to obligations within prayer.
3
Apply the Hanafi principle of amr
The imperative form is the primary evidence. Since none of these acts are prescribed separately outside salah, they must be integrated into the prayer structure. The final sitting is part of that structure, so it inherits the obligation.
4
Consider the Sunnah evidence
The passage states 'He never performed it without the final sitting' – meaning the Prophet consistently performed the final sitting without exception. This constant practice (muwazabah) without omission is evidence of obligation in Hanafi methodology.
5
Contrast with the first sitting
The author notes that the Prophet performed prostrations of forgetfulness when he omitted the first sitting. This indicates the first sitting is not fard (since forgetfulness prostrations are for wajib, not fard). The contrast strengthens the case that the final sitting is fard.
The first sitting is sunnah, not fard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقعدة الأخيرة؛ قال في "فتح القدير": "قوله: (وربك فكبر) [المدثر:3]، وقوله: (وقوموا لله قانتين) [البقرة:238]، وقوله: (فاقرؤوا) [المزمل:20]، وقوله: (اركعوا واسجدوا) [الحج:77]، أوامر ومقتضاها الافتراض، ولم يفرض خارج الصلاة شيء منها، فوجب أن يراد بها الافتراض في الصلاة، وهو لا ينافي إجمال الصلاة. إذ الحاصل حينئذ أنّ الصلاة فعل يشتمل على هذه، بقي كيفية ترتيبها في الأداء، وهل الصلاةُ هذه فقط أو مع أمور أخر، فوقع البيانُ في ذلك كله ببيانه. وقوله: "وهو لم يفعلها قط بدون القعدة الأخيرة"، والموظبة بدون التركِ دليل الوجوب، فإذا وقعت بياناً للفرض المجمل: أعني الصلاة كانت فرضاً متعلقاً بها، ولو لم يقم الدليلُ في غيرها على السنية لكان فرضاً، ولو لم يلزم تقييد مطلق الكتاب بخبر الواحد في الفاتحة، والطمأنينة وهو نسخ للقاطع بالظني، لكانا فرضين. ولولا أنه لم يعد إلى القعدة الأولى لَمَّا سها). ثمَّ عَلِمَ لكانت فرضاً، وعما
And the final sitting. He said in 'Fath al-Qadir': 'His statement: "And your Lord magnify" [al-Muddaththir:3], and His statement: "And stand before Allah devoutly obedient" [al-Baqarah:238], and His statement: "So recite" [al-Muzzammil:20], and His statement: "Bow and prostrate" [al-Hajj:77], are commands and their implication is obligation. Nothing of these was made obligatory outside prayer, so it becomes necessary that they are intended as obligation within prayer. This does not contradict the ambiguity of prayer, because what results is that prayer is an act encompassing these; the manner of their arrangement in performance remained, and whether prayer is only these or with other matters. So clarification occurred in all of that by his explanation. And his statement: 'And he never performed it without the final sitting' – and the constant practice without omission is evidence of obligation. So when it occurs as a clarification of the ambiguous obligation, i.e., prayer, it becomes an obligation related to it. Had the evidence not been established in other matters for being sunnah, it would be obligation. And had it not necessitated restricting the absolute of the Book by a solitary narration in al-Fatihah and tranquility (tuma'ninah) – which is abrogation of the definitive by the speculative – they would be two obligations. And had he not returned to the first sitting when he forgot, then it would be known that it is obligation, and ...'
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof establishing that the final sitting (al-qa'dah al-akhir) in prayer is obligatory (fard). The author quotes from 'Fath al-Qadir', which cites four Quranic verses: 'Magnify your Lord', 'Stand devoutly', 'Recite', and 'Bow and prostrate'. These are commands (awamir) and their default implication in Hanafi usul is obligation. Since none of these acts are prescribed outside of prayer, they must refer to obligations within the prayer. The Prophet's consistent practice of always performing the final sitting (never omitting it) is additional evidence of obligation. The text also addresses potential counterarguments: if other elements (like recitation and tranquility) were proved by solitary narrations, they might not be obligatory due to the principle that a speculative proof cannot abrogate a definitive one. The author also references the case of forgetting the first sitting – the fact that the Prophet performed prostrations of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw) for omitting it indicates it is not fard (since fard omission would require repetition). Thus the final sitting is fard, while the first sitting is not.

Key Terms
القعدة الأخيرة (al-qa'dah al-akhirah): The final sitting in prayer, after the last sujood, wherein the tashahhud is recited.
فرض (fard): An obligatory act; omission invalidates prayer.
أمر (amr): A command; in usul, the imperative form normally indicates obligation unless there is a contrary indicator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary evidence for the obligation of the final sitting?
A) The hadith of the seven limbs
B) The four Quranic verses with imperative forms
C) The consensus of the Sahaba
D) The fact that the Prophet never forgot it

Key Takeaway
The final sitting is a fard pillar of prayer, established by Quranic commands and the Prophet's unwavering practice, distinguishing it from the non-obligatory first sitting.

The Hanafi Concept of Wajib and the Core Recitation Obligations
Commentary defining the wajibat of prayer and their proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of wajib, differentiate it from fard, and identify the proofs for reciting Fatiha and adding a surah in salah.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, a wajib is as binding as fard in practice but established by zanni proof; its intentional omission does not invalidate the prayer but requires repetition.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah begins by defining two key terms from the matn: 'qadr al-tashahhud' and 'al-khuruj bi-sun'ih'. It then explains the nature of wajib as distinct from fard, and lists three specific wajibat of prayer. The first two—reciting al-Fatiha and adding a surah—are supported by ahad hadith. Understanding this distinction is essential for grasping the Hanafi legal hierarchy and the consequences of omission in salah.

Guided Path
1
Define 'wajib' vs 'fard'
Identify from the passage that a wajib is established by a zanni (speculative) proof, is equal to fard in practice, but its denier is not a disbeliever and its intentional omission does not invalidate the prayer.
This is a unique Hanafi distinction; other schools treat all obligations as fard.
2
Define 'qadr al-tashahhud' and 'al-khuruj bi-sun'ih'
Note the correct view that 'qadr al-tashahhud' means the entire tashahhud from start to end, and that 'al-khuruj bi-sun'ih' means any intentional act contrary to prayer after completion.
The author clarifies that additional supplications beyond the tashahhud are sunnah, not wajib.
3
List the three wajibat of salah
From the passage, the three wajibat are: reciting al-Fatiha, adding a surah, and maintaining order (tartib). The first two are discussed in this lesson.
Tartib will be analyzed in the next lesson.
4
Analyze the proofs for Fatiha and surah
The author cites ahad hadith: 'La salata illa bi-Fatiha al-Kitab' (no prayer without the Opening) and 'La salata liman lam yaqra’ bi’l-Hamdi wa suratin ma‘aha' (no prayer for one who does not recite al-Hamd and a surah).
These hadith are from the Six Books, but their transmission is ahad, making the ruling wajib, not fard.
5
Understand the consequence of omission
Forgetting a wajib requires sajdat al-sahw; intentional omission does not invalidate the prayer but requires repetition (i'ada).
This differs from fard, where intentional omission invalidates the act.

The amount of tashahhud, and exiting by his own action. And its obligations: reciting al-Fatiha, adding a surah with it, and maintaining order in what is repeated.
[4] [0] And its obligations: reciting al-Fatiha, adding a surah with it, and maintaining order in what is repeated. We mentioned that prioritizing standing over bowing and bowing over prostration is obligatory (fard) because it is between them likewise.
[1] His saying: 'qadr al-tashahhud' means the amount in which one recites the tashahhud from its beginning to its end. And it is said: the amount in which one says the two words of shahadah. The correct is the first. Thus in 'Jami' al-Mudmarat' and 'al-Binayah'. And in it is an indication that what is added to it of prayer and supplications is not fard but sunnah.
[2] His saying: 'al-khuruj bi-sun'ih' means exiting the prayer intentionally by the performer by a statement or action contrary to the prayer after its completion, whether it be saying 'al-salamu alaykum' as is obligatory, or speech of people, or eating, or drinking, or similar acts that are makruh tahrimi, causing the loss of the wajib. Thus in 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq'.
[3] His saying: 'and its wajib' is that whose obligation is established by a zanni (speculative) proof, and it is equal to fard in terms of practice, except that its denier does not become a disbeliever, and by leaving it forgetfully Sajdat al-Sahw becomes obligatory, and by leaving it intentionally the prayer is not invalidated but repetition is obligatory. Thus mentioned in 'Fath al-Qadir'.
[4] His saying: 'reciting al-Fatiha' due to the hadith: 'No prayer except with the Opening of the Book' and the hadith: 'Every prayer in which Umm al-Quran is not recited is deficient' i.e., incomplete, and other ahad hadiths narrated in the Six Authentic Books.
[5] His saying: 'and adding a surah' i.e., the shortest surah or its equivalent, due to the hadith: 'No prayer for one who does not recite al-Hamd and a surah with it', narrated by al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah and others, and there is discussion in the chapter.
[Page 67] In 'al-Hidayah': 'and maintaining order in what is prescribed repeatedly from actions.' And it is mentioned in the margins of 'al-Hidayah' quoting from 'al-Mabsut' like the second prostration, for if he stood up for the second after having prostrated once, before prostrating the other, he makes it up, and the standing is considered valid because he only omitted a wajib. I say: His saying 'in what is repeated' is not a condition that negates the ruling from other than it, for maintaining order in the pillars that are not repeated in one rak'ah like bowing and the like is also wajib, as will come in the chapter on Sajdat al-Sahw: that Sajdat al-Sahw becomes obligatory due to advancing a pillar... etc., and they cited the analogy of advancing the pillar of bowing before recitation, and Sajdat al-Sahw is only obligatory due to leaving a wajib. So it is known that order between bowing and recitation is wajib, even though they are not repeated in one rak'ah. And it is said in 'al-Dhakhirah': As for advancing the pillar, like bowing before reciting, it is because maintaining order is wajib according to our three imams, contrary to Zufar, for it is fard according to him. So it is known that maintaining order is wajib absolutely, so there is no need for his saying 'in what is repeated'; for this reason I did not mention it in 'al-Mukhtasar'. It is lengthy in 'al-Si'ayah'. If one recites three short verses, or one or two verses that equal three verses, it removes the limit of karahah tahrimiyah necessitated by leaving a wajib. Thus in 'al-Ghunayyah'.
[1] His saying: 'so it is known...' etc.; know that among the actions, some are not repeated in the prayer in the sense of being fard: like the takbir of iftitah, for it is not repeated at all, and like the sitting (qa'dah), for it is not repeated in...
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary expanding on the obligations (wajibat) of prayer as stated in the matn of Al-Wiqayah. The commentator first defines two key terms from the matn: 'qadr al-tashahhud' (the amount of tashahhud) and 'al-khuruj bi-sun'ih' (intentional exit from prayer). Regarding 'qadr al-tashahhud', the correct view is the entire recitation from beginning to end; anything beyond that (like sending blessings) is sunnah, not fard. 'Al-khuruj bi-sun'ih' means deliberately exiting prayer by any act that contradicts it, whether the obligatory salam or other prohibited actions. Next, the author explains the nature of 'wajib' as distinct from 'fard': both are obligatory in practice, but a wajib is established by a speculative (zanni) proof, so its denier is not a disbeliever. Forgetting a wajib requires Sajdat al-Sahw; intentionally omitting it does not invalidate the prayer but requires repetition. The three specific wajibat are then discussed: reciting Surah al-Fatiha (supported by hadith in the Six Books), adding a surah after al-Fatiha (supported by hadith from al-Tirmidhi), and maintaining order (tartib) in repeated acts. The commentary then focuses on the condition 'fima tukurrar' (in what is repeated). The author argues that tartib is wajib in all pillars, not just those that repeat. He cites the example of bowing before recitation: if one bows before reciting, Sajdat al-Sahw is required, which indicates the act omitted was wajib. This is the position of the three main Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), while Zufar considered tartib as fard. The author concludes that the qualifier 'fima tukurrar' is unnecessary, since tartib is wajib absolutely. He also notes that reciting three short verses suffices to fulfill the wajib of adding a surah, avoiding the karahah tahrimiyah of its omission.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): An obligation established by a speculative (zanni) proof; equal to fard in practice but its denier is not a disbeliever, and its omission intentionally does not invalidate the act but requires repetition.
قدر التشهد (qadr al-tashahhud): The amount of time equal to reciting the entire tashahhud from beginning to end; the correct view, as opposed to only the amount for the two shahadas.
الخروج بصنعه (al-khuruj bi-sun'ih): Intentional exit from prayer by the worshipper through a word or action that contradicts the prayer after its completion, whether the obligatory salam or any prohibited act.
سجدة السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness, required when a wajib is omitted forgetfully; it compensates for the deficiency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if someone intentionally omits reciting a surah after al-Fatiha in the first two rak'ahs?
A) The prayer is invalid (batil) and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but must be repeated (i'ada); no sajdat al-sahw.
C) The prayer is valid and no compensation is needed.
D) The prayer is valid but sajdat al-sahw is required even if intentional.

Key Takeaway
Wajibat are as binding as fard in practice but differ in evidence strength and consequences of omission; intentional omission requires repetition but does not invalidate the prayer.

The Obligation of Maintaining Order (Tartib) in Salah: A Hanafi Intra-School Analysis
Expansion and critique of the qualifier on repeated acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi majority consider tartib as wajib (not fard) and evaluate the opposing view of Zufar using the argument from Sajdat al-Sahw.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-Sahw for advancing a pillar proves that the omitted act is wajib, thus tartib is wajib absolutely, not just in repeated actions.

This passage engages in a critical expansion of the matn's phrasing 'fima tukurrar' (in what is repeated). The author argues that maintaining order in all pillars is wajib, using the proof that advancing a pillar (e.g., bowing before recitation) necessitates Sajdat al-Sahw, which only compensates for a wajib. This is contrasted with Zufar's view that tartib is fard. Understanding this intra-school dispute sharpens one's appreciation of usul methodology.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the Hanafi position
The passage discusses whether maintaining order (tartib) among the actions of salah is wajib or fard. The majority of Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold it is wajib.
Zufar alone considers it fard.
2
Present the key proof from Sajdat al-Sahw
If one advances a pillar (e.g., bows before reciting), Sajdat al-Sahw becomes obligatory. Since Sajdat al-Sahw is only required for leaving a wajib, the act that was omitted (recitation before bowing) must be wajib, not fard. Thus, tartib is wajib.
This reasoning applies even to non-repeating actions like bowing and recitation within one rak'ah.
3
Analyze the qualifier 'fima tukurrar'
Al-Hidayah's phrase 'in what is repeated' might suggest that tartib is wajib only for repeating actions (e.g., two prostrations). The author rebuts this by showing that the proof from Sajdat al-Sahw applies to non-repeated actions as well.
The author even omitted the qualifier in his own Mukhtasar.
4
Note Zufar's opposing view
Zufar holds that tartib is fard. His basis is not fully stated, but the author's rebuttal implies that if tartib were fard, then advancing a pillar would invalidate the prayer (since fard omission invalidates), but the ruling is that the prayer is still valid with sajdat al-sahw.
The passage cites al-Dhakhirah attributing the majority view to 'our three imams'.
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that tartib is wajib absolutely. This is supported by the necessity of Sajdat al-Sahw and the consensus of the three major Hanafi imams.
The practical consequence (thamarah) is that intentional or forgetful breach of order does not invalidate the prayer; it only requires sajdat al-sahw if forgetful, or repetition if intentional.

Key Terms
ترتيب (tartib): The correct sequence of actions in salah: standing, recitation, bowing, prostration, sitting, etc.
سجدة السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness, required when a wajib is omitted forgetfully; it compensates for the deficiency.
فيما تكرر (fima tukurrar): The phrase 'in what is repeated' from al-Hidayah, which the author argues is not a restrictive condition.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
The Wujub of Order in Prayer: Wajib or Fard?
Expansion on the wajib status of tartib with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi majority rules that tartib is wajib, identify Zufar's opposing view, and evaluate the legal reasoning based on sajda al-sahw.

Core Idea
Order in prayer is wajib—its omission requires sajda al-sahw, proving it is not fard.

Observing the correct sequence of actions in prayer (tartib) is a fundamental requirement, but is it fard or wajib? The Hanafi school has an internal debate. In this lesson, we examine the sharh on Al-Hidayah that settles this dispute using the rule that sajda al-sahw only compensates for leaving a wajib. By understanding this reasoning, you will grasp how the Hanafi jurists classify obligations and resolve apparent contradictions.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the ruling of the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) on tartib: it is wajib, not fard. Understand that this is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
Wajib = obligatory but less than fard; omission requires sajda al-sahw but does not invalidate prayer.
2
Identify the Opponent and Their View
Recognize that Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) holds tartib as fard. Understand that fard = fundamental; omission invalidates prayer.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; both sides agree on the requirement, but differ on the degree.
3
Follow the Hanafi Proof
Trace the evidence: 1) Sajda al-sahw is only wajib for leaving a wajib, not a fard. 2) Examples like bowing before recitation (advancing a pillar) require sajda al-sahw. 3) Therefore, the missed element (order) must be wajib.
The proof is based on the talil (reasoning) from the rules of sajda al-sahw.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response to Zufar
Note that the author rejects Zufar's view by emphasizing that the matn's phrase 'in what is repeated' is not restrictive. He cites Al-Dhakhira and examples from sajda al-sahw to show that order is wajib absolutely, even for actions repeated across the whole prayer.
The author also critiques commentators who restrict 'repeated' to within a rak'a, arguing that this contradicts the examples where sajda al-sahw is required for delaying an action repeated across the prayer.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Work out the practical consequence: if one intentionally bows before reciting, according to the three imams, the prayer is valid but requires sajda al-sahw; according to Zufar, the prayer is invalid. In practice, the mufta bihi (wajib) is followed.
This difference affects how a mufti advises someone who made a mistake in prayer order.

Source Text

في «الهداية»: ومراعاة الترتيب فيما شُرعَ مكرراً من الأفعال). وذُكِرَ في حواشي ((الهداية» نقلاً عن «المبسوط» (۲) : كالسجدة الثانية، فإنه لو قام إلى الثانية بعدما سجد سجدة واحدة، قبل أن يسجد الأخرى يقضيها، ويكون القيام معتبراً ؛ لأنه لم يترك إلا الواجب. أقول : قوله : فيما تكرّر ليس قيداً يُوجب نفي الحكم عما عداه ، فإنَّه مراعاة الترتيب في الأركان التي لا تتكرر في ركعة واحدة كالركوع ونحوه واجب أيضاً على ما يأتي في باب سجود السهو : أن سجود السهو يَجِبُ بتقديم ركن... إلى آخره، وأوردوا نظير تقديم الرُّكنِ الرُّكوعَ قبل القرءاة، وسجدة السهو لا تجب إلا بترك الواجب ، فَعُلِمَ أَنَّ الترتيب بين الركوع والقرءاة واجب، مع أنهما غير مكرّرين في ركعة واحدة. وقد قال في «الذخيرة»: أما تقديمُ الرُّكن نحو أن يركع قبل أن يقرأ ؛ فلأن مراعاة الترتيب واجبة عند أصحابنا الثَّلاثة خلافاً لَزُفَر له، فإنَّها فرض عنده. فَعُلِمَ أنَّ مراعاة الترتيب واجبةٌ مطلقاً ، فلا حاجة إلى قوله فيما تكرر ؛ ولهذا لم أذكره في «المختصر » (۳). [١] قوله : فعلم.... الخ ؛ اعلم أنّ من الأفعالِ ما لا يتكرر في الصلاة على سبيل الفرضية : كتكبير الافتتاح ؛ فإنّه غير متكرّر أصلاً، وكالقعدة فإنها غير متكرّرة في الثنائية، وفي الرباعية والثلاثيّة وإن تكرّرت ، لكن الأولى واجبة، والترتيب بين هذه الأفعال فرض حتى لو أخَّرَ تكبيرة الافتتاح عن القعدة بطلت صلاته، والترتيب بينها وبين غيرها من الأفعال أيضاً فرض، لكن لا بمعنى أنه تفسد الصلاة بتركه، بل بمعنى أنه لا يعتد به ، فلو تذكر بعد القعدة قبل السلام أو بعده أنه ترك سجدة أو ركوعاً أو غير ذلك . الأفعال السابقة، لزم عليه أن يأتي به ويتشهد ثانياً، ويسجد للسهو. كذا في من «البزازية» و«فتاوی قاضي خان». ومن الأفعال ما يتحد في كل ركعة ويتعدد في كلّ الصلاة ؛ كالقيام والركوع والقراءة، ومنها : ما يتعدد في كل ركعة كالسجدة. إذا عرفت هذا فاعرف أنّ القسم الأول ليس مراداً قطعـاً مـن قـولـهـم عند ذكـر واجبات الصلاة : ورعاية الترتيب فيما تكرر» ؛ لعدم تكراره، بقي القسمان الأخيران، فذهب كثير من شراح «الهداية» وغيرها إلى أنّ المراد ما تكرر في كل ركعة احترازاً عما تكرّر في الصلاة دون الركعة، فإنّ الترتيب بين ما تكرّر في كل الصلاة فرض لا واجب، كما هو مصرح في «فتح القدير» و«الكافي» وغيرهما. وأورد عليهم الشارحُ له بأنه ليس قيداً احترازياً يحترز به عما تكرر في كل الصلاة، وظنّ أنّ الترتيب بين الأفعال المتكررة مطلقاً واجب تكرّرت في كل ركعة أو في كل الصلاة، واستند بعباراتهم الواقعة في باب سجود السهو، حيث مثلوا الصور التي يجب فيها سجود السهو بما يترك فيه الترتيب بين الأفعال المتكرّرة في الصلاة الغير المتكررة في الركعة. (1) ومن المعلوم أن سجدة السهو لا تجب إلا بترك الواجب لا بترك الفرض، وأشار إلى إيرادِ لزوم التناقض بين كلماتهم في باب صفة الصلاة»، حيث يصرحون أنَّ المراد بما تكرر المتكرّر في كلِّ ركعة، وأنه احتراز عن المتكرّر في كلّ الصلاة، وأنّ الترتيب بينه فرض، وبين كلماتهم في «باب سجود السهو».
In Al-Hidayah: 'And observing the order in what is prescribed as repeated among actions.' And it is mentioned in the glosses of Al-Hidayah, quoting from Al-Mabsut: Like the second prostration, for if he stood up for the second [raka] after performing one prostration, before performing the other, he makes it up [later], and the standing is considered valid; because he only left an obligatory [action]. I say: His statement 'in what is repeated' is not a restrictive condition that negates the ruling from other than it, for observing order in the pillars that are not repeated in one raka, like bowing and similar, is also obligatory, as will come in the chapter of the prostration of forgetfulness: that the prostration of forgetfulness is required for advancing a pillar... etc., and they cited as an example advancing the pillar of bowing before recitation, and the prostration of forgetfulness is only required for leaving an obligatory [action], so it is known that order between bowing and recitation is obligatory, even though they are not repeated in one raka. And it is said in Al-Dhakhira: As for advancing a pillar, such as bowing before reciting; because observing order is obligatory according to our three [imams], contrary to Zufar, for whom it is fard. So it is known that observing order is obligatory absolutely, so there is no need for his statement 'in what is repeated'; and for this reason I did not mention it in Al-Mukhtasar. [1] His statement: 'so it is known...' etc.; know that among actions are those that are not repeated in the prayer as fard: like the takbir of opening, for it is not repeated at all, and like the sitting, for it is not repeated in a two-raka prayer, and in four-raka or three-raka prayers, though it is repeated, the first [sitting] is obligatory, and order between these actions is fard, such that if he delays the takbir of opening after the sitting, his prayer is invalid. And order between them and other actions is also fard, but not in the sense that the prayer becomes invalid by leaving it, but in the sense that it is not considered [valid]. So if he remembers after the sitting, before or after the salam, that he left a prostration or bowing or other previous actions, he must perform [the missed action] and recite the tashahhud a second time, and perform the prostration of forgetfulness. This is from Al-Bazzaziyya and Fatawa Qadi Khan. Among actions are those that are uniform in each raka and repeated in the entire prayer: like standing, bowing, and recitation; and among them are those that are repeated in each raka, like prostration. If you understand this, then know that the first category is definitely not intended by their statement when mentioning the obligations of prayer: 'and observing order in what is repeated'; because it is not repeated. There remain the last two categories. Many commentators of Al-Hidayah and others hold that what is meant is what is repeated in each raka, as a precautionary restriction against what is repeated in the prayer but not in the raka, for order between what is repeated in the entire prayer is fard, not wajib, as is explicitly stated in Fath al-Qadir, Al-Kafi, and others. The commentator [of Al-Hidayah] objected to them that it is not a precautionary restriction to guard against what is repeated in the entire prayer, and he thought that order between repeated actions absolutely is wajib, whether they are repeated in each raka or in the entire prayer, and he relied on their statements in the chapter of the prostration of forgetfulness, where they exemplified the cases in which the prostration of forgetfulness is required by the omission of order between actions that are repeated in the prayer but not repeated in the raka. And it is known that the prostration of forgetfulness is only required by leaving a wajib, not by leaving a fard. And he pointed to the occurrence of contradiction between their statements in the chapter 'Description of Prayer', where they explicitly state that what is meant by 'what is repeated' is what is repeated in each raka, and that it is a precautionary restriction against what is repeated in the entire prayer, and that order between it is fard, and between their statements in the chapter 'Prostration of Forgetfulness'.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the matn of Al-Hidayah regarding the ruling of observing order (tartib) in the actions of prayer. The author, commenting on the phrase 'in what is repeated', clarifies that this condition is not restrictive; rather, observing order in all actions, whether repeated in a single rak'a or across the whole prayer, is generally wajib (obligatory but not fard). He cites examples: if one stands up for the second rak'a after only one sajda, the standing is valid because only a wajib (the second sajda) was missed, requiring qada later. The order between bowing and recitation is wajib, as missing it necessitates sajda al-sahw, which is only required for leaving a wajib, not a fard. He then presents the intra-Hanafi dispute: according to the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), order is wajib; Zufar holds it is fard. The author argues that order is absolutely wajib, so the matn's phrase 'in what is repeated' is unnecessary. He then categorizes actions: (1) non-repeated like takbirat al-ihram and the first sitting in a two-rak'a prayer—order here is fard such that delaying takbir causes invalidity; (2) repeated in each rak'a like sujud; (3) repeated across the whole prayer but not within a rak'a like standing, bowing, recitation. Many commentators say the matn refers only to category (2) to avoid confusion with category (3), where order is fard. However, the author of this sharh rejects that interpretation, stating that order in all repeated actions is wajib, citing examples from sajda al-sahw where the missed order is between actions repeated across the prayer but not within a rak'a, yet sajda al-sahw is wajib. Thus, the matn's phrase is general, and the later distinction is contradictory. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that tartib is wajib absolutely, as per the three imams, and this is the view of the majority.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tartib): Observing the correct sequence of actions in prayer as prescribed by the Shari'a.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory duty that is less than fard; leaving it requires compensation (sajda al-sahw) but does not invalidate the prayer.
فرض (fard): A fundamental obligation; intentional omission invalidates the prayer; accidental omission requires repetition of that action if possible.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness (sahw) in prayer due to omission, addition, or doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (three imams), what is the ruling on observing order (tartib) between bowing and recitation?
A) Fard, because it is a pillar of prayer.
B) Wajib, because sajda al-sahw is required if missed.
C) Sunnah, because it is recommended but not required.
D) Makruh, because delaying recitation is disliked.

Key Takeaway
Order in prayer is wajib, not fard, because its omission requires sajda al-sahw, which compensates only for leaving a wajib.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
12 min
Order Between Repeated Actions: Fard vs Wajib Classification
Intra-Hanafi dispute on classification of order between repeated prayer actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between cases where order (tartib) in prayer is fard (invalidates) versus wajib (requires sajda al-sahw) and apply al-Bahr al-Raiq's reconciliation to resolve apparent contradictions in Hanafi texts.

Core Idea
Order between actions repeated per rak'ah is wajib; between the seven fard actions repeated across the whole prayer is fard.

In the Hanafi school, a clear distinction between fard and wajib is essential, especially in prayer rulings. This lesson examines a debate among Hanafi scholars: is the order (tartib) between actions that repeat in prayer always fard, or is it sometimes hanya wajib? By understanding the resolution given by al-Bahr al-Raiq, you will learn to classify order violations correctly and avoid confusion when studying different chapters of fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of repeated actions
Actions in prayer are either repeated in every rak'ah (like sujud) or repeated across the whole prayer but not per rak'ah (like qiyam, ruku', takbir). Classify which category each action belongs to.
This classification is the foundation of the dispute.
2
State the conflicting positions
Many Hanafi commentators (including author of Fath al-Qadir) hold that order between actions repeated per rak'ah is wajib, while order between the seven fard actions (which repeat across the prayer) is fard. Opposing scholars (like al-Sharih and al-Birjandi) argue order is always wajib, citing examples from Bab Sajdah al-Sahw.
The conflict arises from seemingly contradictory statements in different fiqh chapters.
3
Analyze the 'fard' vs 'wajib' usage in different contexts
In 'Bab Sifat al-Salah', when scholars say 'order is fard', it means the pillar itself is invalidated if order is violated, requiring repetition of that pillar. In 'Bab Sajdah al-Sahw', when they say 'order is wajib', it means if the pillar is repeated correctly, the formal violation of order requires sajda al-sahw but does not invalidate the prayer.
This is the key to al-Bahr al-Raiq's reconciliation.
4
Apply the reconciliation to sample scenarios
For example, if someone prostrates before bowing (violating order in actions repeated per rak'ah), they must repeat the bow then the prostration, and perform sajda al-sahw. If someone delays takbirat al-iftitah after the final sitting (violating order among the seven fard actions), the prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
The practical consequence (thamarah) is different for each category.
5
Evaluate al-Birjandi's alternative interpretation
Al-Birjandi claimed that 'fard' in 'Sifat al-Salah' actually means 'wajib'. The author and al-Bahr al-Raiq reject this because it undermines the scholars' explicit distinction between actions repeated per rak'ah and across the prayer. Acknowledge why the majority view is mufta bihi.
This step sharpens your critical evaluation of scholarly opinions.

For the two-rak'ah prayer, and in the four- and three-rak'ah prayers, even if it is repeated, the first is obligatory, and the order between these actions is fard, such that if he delays the takbirat al-iftitah after the sitting, his prayer becomes invalid. And the order between them and other actions is also fard, but not in the sense that the prayer becomes invalid by leaving it; rather, in the sense that it is not considered valid. So if after the sitting, before or after the salutation, he remembers that he left a prostration or a bow or something else of the previous actions, he must perform it, repeat the tashahhud, and perform sajda al-sahw. Thus it is in al-Bazzaziyya and Fatawa Qadi Khan. Among the actions, some are single in each rak'ah and multiple in the entire prayer, like standing, bowing, and recitation; and some are multiple in each rak'ah, like prostration. When you know this, then know that the first category is definitely not intended by their statement when mentioning the obligations of prayer: "Observance of order in what is repeated"; because it has no repetition. The last two categories remain. Many commentators of al-Hidayah and others held that what is intended is what is repeated in every rak'ah, as a precaution against what is repeated in the prayer but not in the rak'ah, for the order between what is repeated in the entire prayer is fard, not wajib, as is clearly stated in Fath al-Qadir, al-Kafi, and others. The commentator (al-Sharih) objected to them, saying that it is not a restrictive condition to exclude what is repeated in the entire prayer, and he thought that the order between repeated actions absolutely is wajib, whether repeated in every rak'ah or in the entire prayer, relying on their statements in the chapter of Sajdah al-Sahw, where they gave examples of situations in which sajda al-sahw is obligatory, such as when the order between actions repeated in the prayer but not repeated in the rak'ah is omitted. And it is well known that sajda al-sahw is only obligatory for leaving a wajib, not for leaving a fard. He indicated the contradiction between their statements in the chapter "Description of Prayer", where they state that what is intended by "what is repeated" is that which repeats in every rak'ah, and it is a precaution against what is repeated in the entire prayer, and that the order between them is fard, and between their statements in the chapter of Sajdah al-Sahw. It occurs to me that what is intended by "what is repeated" is that which repeats in the prayer, as a precaution against what does not repeat in the prayer as a fard, namely takbirat al-iftitah and the last sitting, for observance of order in them is fard. The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq responded: "There is no contradiction between the two statements; because their statement here 'the order between what is repeated in the prayer is a condition or fard' means that the pillar in which it occurs becomes invalid by its omission, such that if he bows after prostrating, it is not counted as valid by consensus, as stated in al-Nihaya, so he must repeat the prostration. And their statement in the chapter of Sajdah al-Sahw, 'this order is wajib,' means that the prayer does not become invalid by its omission if he repeats the pillar he performed, and if he repeats it, then he has omitted the order in form, so sajda al-sahw is required." End. This is a good verification that resolves the apparent contradiction among their statements, and it becomes correct that "what is repeated" in the sense of what repeats in every rak'ah is a restrictive condition. As for interpreting their statements in the chapter of "Description of Prayer" such that what is meant by fard applied to what is repeated in the prayer is actually wajib, as al-Birjandi did in Sharh al-Nuqaya, it is not correct; their statements reject this. How so? If so, it would not be valid for them to make "what is repeated" in the sense of what repeats in every rak'ah as a precaution against it. 1) His statement: "It occurs" is from khutur, bab nasara yansuru. "To me" means it passes and occurs in my mind. The purpose of it is to explain their statement "what is repeated" such that it is a restrictive condition. It is objected: Since their statement has a sound interpretation, why did he omit it in al-Mukhtasar? And how can his previous statement, "There is no need for it," be correct? The answer: The occurrence of this explanation was after the composition of al-Mukhtasar, and the lack of need for it is in terms of a precaution against what is repeated in the entire prayer, not absolutely. And in this context, there are investigations and subtleties that we have detailed in al-Si'aya.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage discusses the Hanafi classification of order (tartib) between actions in prayer. It distinguishes between fard (obligatory that invalidates the prayer if omitted) and wajib (necessary, but omission requires sajda al-sahw without invalidating the prayer). The author begins by stating that order between the seven fard actions of prayer (like takbirat al-iftitah, qiyam, ruku', sujud, etc.) is fard; delaying one fard action relative to another, e.g., delaying takbir after the sitting, invalidates the prayer. However, if one omits a wajib action like a prostration and remembers after sitting, he must perform it, repeat tashahhud, and do sajda al-sahw. Then he categorizes actions: some occur once per rak'ah but multiple times in the whole prayer (like standing, bowing, recitation), and some occur multiple times per rak'ah (like prostration). He notes that when scholars say 'observance of order in what is repeated' among the wajibat of prayer, they mean actions repeated in every rak'ah, not those repeated only in the whole prayer. Many commentators of Al-Hidayah hold that order between actions repeated per rak'ah is wajib (not fard), while order between actions repeated across the whole prayer (like the seven fard actions) is fard—a view in Fath al-Qadir and al-Kafi. A commentator (al-Sharih) objected, claiming order between repeated actions is always wajib, based on examples in the chapter of sajda al-sahw where sajda is required for violating order between actions repeated in the prayer but not per rak'ah. However, sajda al-sahw is only for wajib omission, not fard. The author then mentions his own thought: perhaps 'what is repeated' refers to what repeats in the prayer generally, except for takbirat al-iftitah and the last sitting, where order is fard. But al-Bahr al-Raiq provides a conclusive reconciliation: when scholars in 'Description of Prayer' say order is fard, they mean the pillar itself becomes invalid, so it must be repeated; but if the pillar is repeated correctly, the order is only formally violated, requiring sajda al-sahw. Hence there is no contradiction. The author rejects al-Birjandi's interpretation that 'fard' in that context actually means 'wajib', because that would undermine the distinction made by many scholars.

Key Terms
الترتيب (al-tartib): Order or sequence prescribed between actions in prayer.
ما تكرر (ma takarara): That which is repeated; in this context, actions that occur multiple times in the prayer, either per rak'ah or across the whole prayer.
الفرض (al-fard): Strict obligation; omission invalidates the prayer or the specific pillar.
الواجب (al-wajib): Necessary act; omission does not invalidate the prayer but requires sajda al-sahw.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, what is the ruling on order (tartib) between actions that repeat in every rak'ah (e.g., between two prostrations)?
A) It is fard; violation invalidates the prayer.
B) It is wajib; violation requires sajda al-sahw but does not invalidate the prayer.
C) It is sunnah; violation does not require anything.
D) It is haram; violation is prohibited.

Key Takeaway
Order in prayer is not monolithic: distinguish between wajib (per rak'ah actions, sajda suffices) and fard (seven pillars across prayer, violation invalidates).

The First Sitting: Wajib or Sunnah? The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on obligation of first sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds the first sitting and its tashahhud as wajib, identify the opposing view of al-Karkhi and al-Tahawi, and evaluate the evidence for each position.

Core Idea
The first sitting is wajib because ahad hadith and sajda sahw prove it is not fard but still obligatory.

Prayer has many components, some obligatory (fard), some necessary (wajib), and some recommended (sunnah). One of the debated elements among Hanafi scholars is the first sitting (al-qa'dah al-ula) and the recitation of tashahhud during it. While some early Hanafis considered it sunnah, the majority of the school and the relied-upon view is that it is wajib. This lesson unpacks the evidence and reasoning behind this ruling, focusing on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and the Prophet's sajda sahw.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the ruling of the first sitting and tashahhud according to the majority. What level is it? (fard/wajib/sunnah)
2
Identify the Opponent
Which Hanafi scholars held a different view? What did they consider it?
Al-Karkhi and al-Tahawi are named.
3
Follow the Opponent's Proof
What evidence did al-Karkhi and al-Tahawi use to argue sunnah?
They relied on the lack of explicit mention in some narrations and the fact that the Prophet's omission could indicate it is not mandatory.
4
Analyse the Hanafi Response
How does the majority rebut this view? Which hadith and usul principles are cited?
The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud commanding tashahhud in every sitting, and the usul principle that whatever is necessary for a wajib is itself wajib.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
What practical difference does it make if the first sitting is wajib vs sunnah? How does sajda sahw relate?
If wajib, forgetting requires sajda sahw; if sunnah, no compensation is needed.
