Placing Hands Under the Navel in Prayer: Evidence and Method
Ruling on hand placement in prayer with hadith evidence and intra-school discussion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on hand placement in prayer, cite the primary hadith evidence, and explain the intra-school difference regarding placing vs. grasping and the exact location.

Core Idea
The sunnah is to place hands under the navel; the evidence is the sound hadith of Wail ibn Hujr.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on hand placement during the standing posture in prayer. While many Muslims are aware that Hanafis place their hands under the navel, fewer know the precise evidence and the scholarly debates over method (placing vs grasping) and location (forearm vs wrist). By studying this passage, you will learn the key hadith proofs and the tarjih within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the ruling is about (hand placement in prayer) and its hukm level (sunnah, not wajib).
The passage discusses both the action and its sunnah status.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the hadith that forms the main evidence for placing hands under the navel. The passage mentions the hadith of Wail ibn Hujr.
The chain of this hadith is defended by the author.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the hadith proves the ruling: the Prophet's explicit action (placing right hand on left under navel) indicates the recommended practice.
The hadith uses the word 'under the navel' explicitly.
4
Note the intra-school ikhtilaf
Identify the differing opinions among Hanafi scholars: placing vs grasping, and forearm vs wrist. The passage also mentions the objection of Shurunbulali and Nabulsi to a certain combination.
Al-Binaayah favors the wrist joint based on the hadith.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Determine the mufta bihi position: placing the right hand on the left under the navel, either by placing the palm or grasping, and the location is the wrist joint.
The preferred view is from al-Binaayah, which is supported by the hadith of Wail.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٢] قوله : ويضع يمينه على شماله ; ورد في بعض الروايات : «أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وضع يمينه على شماله» أخرجه أبو داود وابن خزيمة وابن حبان، وفي بعضها: «إنّه قبض بيمينه على شماله» أخرجه النسائي، وفي بعضها: «أخذ شماله بيمينه»، أخرجه أبو داود وابن حبان. فذهب بعض مشايخنا إلى اختيار الجمع بأن يضع باطن كفه اليمنى على ظاهرِ كفه اليُسرى، ويُحلّق بالخنصر والإبهام على الرسغ ، ليتحقق القبضُ والوضع كلاهما. وأورد عليه الشرنبلالي والنابلسي وغيرهما بأن هذا جمع خارج عن المذهب والأحاديث، والمختار أن يضع تارةً ويقبض تارة، ثم محل الوضع قيل ذراعه الأيسر، وقيل مفصله الأيسر، قال في «البناية»: وهو الأصح ، ويوافقه حديث وائل : «أنه وضع يده اليمنى على ظهر كفّه اليسرى والرسغ والساعد». ثم تحت سرته : كالقنوتِ وصلاة الجنازة، ويرسل في قومة الركوع لقوله : تحت سرته ; لما أخرجه أبو داود وابن أبي شيبة والدارقطني والبيهقي عن علي قال : «من السنة وضع الكفّ على الكف في الصلاة تحت السرة ) ، وسنده ضعيف. وأخرج ابن أبي شيبة عن وكيع عن موسى بن عمير عن علقمة بن وائل بن حجر عن أبيه قال : «رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وضع يمينه على شماله في الصلاة تحت السرة ، وسنده جيد، ورواته كلهم ثقات فوكيع أحد الأعلام وموسى وثقه أبو حاتم ، وأخرج له النسائي، وعلقمة أخرجَ له البخاري في كتاب «رفع اليدين»، ومسلم والأربعة وثقه ابن حبان، فهو شاهد لحديث علي ، كذا في تخريج أحاديث الاختيار شرح المختار» لقاسم ابن قطلوبغا). فإن قلت : إن فيه انقطاعاً ; لأنَّ علقمة لم يسمع من أبيه، بل ولد بعد موت أبيه بستة أشهر. قلت : هذا قول بعض المحدثين، والصحيح أنّ المولود بعد أبيه هو أخوه عبد الجبار، وأمّا علقمة فقد حدَّث عن أبيه ، وسمع منه كما لا يخفى على من طالع «سنن النسائي»، و«جامع الترمذي»، وقد نقّحت هذا البحث في رسالتي : «القول الجازم في سقوط الحد بنكاح المحارم».
[2] His saying: 'And he places his right hand on his left'; it has been reported in some narrations: 'That the Prophet (peace be upon him) placed his right hand on his left' – reported by Abu Dawud, Ibn Khuzaymah, and Ibn Hibban. And in some: 'He grasped his right hand on his left' – reported by al-Nasa'i. And in some: 'He took his left hand with his right' – reported by Abu Dawud and Ibn Hibban. So some of our early scholars chose to combine by placing the palm of the right hand on the back of the left hand, and forming a ring with the little finger and thumb on the wrist, so that both grasping and placing are realized. But al-Shurunbulali, al-Nabulsi, and others objected to this, saying this combination is outside the madhhab and the hadith, and the chosen view is to place sometimes and grasp sometimes. Then the place of placement is said to be the left forearm, and it is said his left wrist joint. He said in al-Binaayah: it is the most correct, and the hadith of Wail supports it: 'He placed his right hand on the back of his left hand, the wrist, and the forearm.' Then: 'Under his navel' – like in qunut and funeral prayer, and he releases in the standing after bowing. For his saying: 'Under his navel' – because of what Abu Dawud, Ibn Abi Shaybah, al-Daraqutni, and al-Bayhaqi narrated from Ali: 'It is from the sunnah to place the palm on the palm in prayer under the navel' – and its chain is weak. And Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated from Waki' from Musa ibn Umayr from Alqamah ibn Wail ibn Hujr from his father: 'I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) place his right hand on his left in prayer under the navel' – and its chain is sound, and all its narrators are trustworthy, for Waki' is one of the leading scholars, and Musa was declared trustworthy by Abu Hatim, and al-Nasa'i narrated from him, and Alqamah was narrated from by al-Bukhari in the book 'Raf' al-Yadayn', and Muslim and the four (Sunan authors) and he was declared trustworthy by Ibn Hibban, so it is a witness for the hadith of Ali. Thus in the takhrij of Ahadith al-Ikhtiyar Sharh al-Mukhtar by Qasim ibn Qatlubugha. If you say: there is a discontinuity in it because Alqamah did not hear from his father, rather he was born six months after his father's death. I say: this is the statement of some hadith scholars, but the correct view is that the one born after his father is his brother Abd al-Jabbar, while Alqamah did narrate from his father and heard from him, as is not hidden from those who examine Sunan al-Nasa'i and Jami' al-Tirmidhi. And I have detailed this research in my treatise: 'al-Qawl al-Jazim fi Suqut al-Hadd bi Nikah al-Mahrim'.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage provides the evidence for the Hanafi ruling of placing hands under the navel in prayer. It begins by citing hadith narrations: the Prophet (ﷺ) placed his right hand on his left, in some versions he grasped, in others he took. Some Hanafi scholars suggested combining placing and grasping by placing the palm on the back and forming a ring with the little finger and thumb around the wrist. However, Shurunbulali and Nabulsi criticized this as departing from the school and the hadith. The correct view is to sometimes place and sometimes grasp. The placement is on the left forearm or the left wrist joint, with al-Binaayah stating the latter is more correct, supported by the hadith of Wail. Then the specific location under the navel is mentioned: for qunut and funeral prayer, and in the standing after bowing (qawmah) the hands are released. The proof for under the navel is the hadith of Ali (weak chain) and the sound hadith of Wail. The author defends the chain of Wail, addressing the objection that Alqamah did not hear from his father, clarifying that it is his brother Abd al-Jabbar who was born after his father's death, while Alqamah did hear from his father.

Key Terms
السرة (al-surrah): The navel, the specific point below which hands are placed in prayer according to Hanafis.
القبض (al-qabḍ): Grasping the left wrist with the right hand, as opposed to simply placing the palm on the back.
الرسغ (al-rusgh): The wrist joint, the part of the wrist where the hand meets the forearm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which hadith does the passage use to support placing hands under the navel?
A) Hadith of Ali with a weak chain
B) Hadith of Wail with a sound chain
C) Hadith of Anas about prayer
D) The Quranic verse on prayer

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school relies on the sound hadith of Wail ibn Hujr to establish placing the right hand on the left under the navel as a sunnah in prayer.

Evidence for Placing Hands Under the Navel
Ruling with hadith proof for hand placement under navel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi proof for placing hands under the navel in prayer and defend its reliability against the objection of discontinuity.

Core Idea
The Hanafi hand placement under the navel is established by a good hadith from Wail ibn Hujr, witnessed by Ali's report.

In this passage, the commentator presents the Hanafi evidence for placing the hands under the navel during prayer. Two hadiths are cited: one from Ali (weak chain) and a stronger one from Wail ibn Hujr via his son Alqamah. The commentary then addresses and refutes an objection about a discontinuity in the chain, affirming the validity of the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage rules on the placement of hands (right over left) during the standing posture in prayer. Determine the legal classification (sunnah) and the specific position: under the navel.
The ruling is sunnah, not wajib, based on the nature of the evidence.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the two hadiths cited: the hadith of Ali (weak chain) and the hadith of Wail ibn Hujr (good chain). Note how the commentator evaluates their chains.
The weak hadith is supported by the stronger one, which is called a 'shahid' (witness).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Identify which phrase in the hadith directly indicates the ruling. The explicit phrase 'under the navel' (tahta al-surra) specifies the location.
The imperative 'placing' in the context of sunnah implies recommendation, not obligation.
4
Analyze the objection and response
The commentator anticipates a criticism: that Alqamah did not hear from his father. The response clarifies that Alqamah did hear from Wail, while his brother Abd al-Jabbar was the one born after Wail's death. This preserves the continuity (ittisal) of the chain.
This is a classic example of a scholar defending a hadith's chain against a claim of inqita' (discontinuity).
5
Determine the mufta bihi and note ikhtilaf
The Hanafi school relies on this evidence and places hands under the navel. The Shafi'i school places them on the chest. Note that the Hanafi ruling is sunnah and based on the preponderance of evidence.
The difference is practical: the position of hands during prayer.

Under his navel: like the qunut and funeral prayer, and he releases (his hands) during the qawma of bowing.
1. For the statement 'under his navel': due to what Abu Dawud, Ibn Abi Shaybah, al-Daraqutni, and al-Bayhaqi narrated from Ali who said: 'It is from the sunnah to place the palm upon the palm in prayer under the navel,' and its chain is weak.
(2) And Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated from Waki‘ from Musa ibn ‘Umair from ‘Alqamah ibn Wa’il ibn Hujr from his father who said: 'I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) place his right hand on his left in prayer under the navel,' and its chain is good, and its narrators are all trustworthy: Waki‘ is one of the imams, and Musa was declared trustworthy by Abu Hatim, and al-Nasa’i narrated from him, and ‘Alqamah: al-Bukhari narrated from him in the book 'Raising the Hands', and Muslim and the four (Sunan) and Ibn Hibban declared him trustworthy. So it is a witness to the hadith of Ali. This is as in 'Takhrij Ahadith al-Ikhtiyar Sharh al-Mukhtar' (3) by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha.
If you say: There is a discontinuity in it because ‘Alqamah did not hear from his father; rather he was born six months after his father’s death. I say: This is the saying of some hadith scholars, but the correct view is that the one born after his father was his brother ‘Abd al-Jabbar; as for ‘Alqamah, he narrated from his father and heard from him, as is not hidden from one who reads 'Sunan al-Nasa’i' and 'Jami‘ al-Tirmidhi'. And I have investigated this research in my treatise 'al-Qawl al-Jazim fi Suqut al-Hadd bi Nikah al-Maharam'.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof for the Hanafi position of placing hands under the navel during prayer. The author begins by stating the ruling: the hands are placed under the navel, similar to the qunut and funeral prayer, and they are released during the qawma (rising from bowing). He then provides evidence: the hadith of Ali (ra) that 'it is from the sunnah to place the palm upon the palm in prayer under the navel,' though he notes its chain is weak. He then presents a stronger hadith from Wail ibn Hujr via his son Alqamah, with a chain evaluated as good. He addresses the objection that Alqamah did not hear from his father, clarifying that Alqamah did hear from him, and it was his brother Abd al-Jabbar who was born after Wail's death. Thus, the hadith is valid evidence for the Hanafi practice.

Key Terms
تحت سرته (tahta surratihi): Under his navel, referring to the placement of the hands during standing in prayer.
قومة الركوع (qawmat al-ruku‘): The standing after rising from bowing.
إرسال (irsal): Releasing or leaving the hands hanging down (not clasped).

The General Rule for Hand Placement and Reciting Thana in Prayer
Explains when to place hands and the recitation of thana'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for hand placement in prayer based on the presence of prescribed dhikr, and recite thana' correctly.

Core Idea
Hands are placed during any standing that includes a prescribed lengthy dhikr; otherwise, they are released.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains two key elements of the prayer: when to place hands during the standing positions and how to recite thana'. The author sets out a general principle linking hand placement to the presence of a prescribed remembrance, and then clarifies that 'masnun' here means 'prescribed' broadly, not just the technical sunnah. Understanding this principle helps you navigate different postures in prayer systematically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The passage states: every standing that contains a prescribed remembrance requires hand placement; otherwise, hands are released. This is the core principle.
The Arabic: 'كل قيام فيه ذكر مسنون ففيه الوضع'
2
Determine which standings contain prescribed dhikr
Standings with lengthy prescribed dhikr include: after the opening takbir (for thana', ta'awwudh, basmalah, Fatihah, surah), during qunut, and between the additional takbirs of Eid. In these, hands are placed.
The passage mentions 'ذكر مسنون' includes wajib, fard, and sunnah in a broad sense.
3
Exclude standings with short dhikr
The qawma (rising from ruku') contains only the short phrases 'sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' and 'rabbana lakal hamd'. Since the dhikr is short, hands are not placed.
The commentary cites Ilyas Zadah distinguishing long vs. short dhikr.
4
Apply the principle to Eid prayer
Between the additional takbirs of Eid, hands are placed because takbir is a prescribed dhikr. After the takbirs are completed in the second rak'ah, hands are not placed again before bowing.
The text references 'Majalis al-Abrar' for this detail.
5
Note the distinction for women
The Hanafi school places hands on the chest for women, based on the hadith of Wail ibn Hujr (which the Shafi'is follow for all), for greater modesty.
This is an exception to the general rule for men.

وبين تكبيرات العيدين) ، فالحاصل أن كل قيام" فيه ذكر مسنون" ففيه
الوضع، وكُل قيام ليس كذا ففيه الإرسال.
[٤]
(ثم يثني )
وبالجملة؛ فليس وضع اليدين تحت السرِّةِ كما يظنّه الظانون أنه ليس له دليل
(۱)
معتد به ، نعم قد ثبت عن النبي الا الله وضع اليدين فوق السرة عند الصدر (١) أيضاً في رواية أحمد وابن خزيمة، وبه أخذ الشافعي الله ومن تبعه، وأخذ به أصحابنا في حق النساء؛ لأنَّ وضع اليدين على الصدر أستر لهنّ، وللتفصيل موضع آخر.
[١] قوله : وبين تكبيرات العيدين؛ أي السنة الزوائد، وأما بعدها ففي الركعة الأولى يضع ويقرأ بعد الثلاثة، وفي الركعة الثانية إذا فرغ من الزوائد وكبر للركوع من غير وضع صرح به في مجالس الابرار».
(٢) قوله : قيام؛ أي حقيقي أو حكمي، كما إذا صلى قاعداً، كذا قال على القاري في «شرح النقاية»(٢).
[٣]قوله : مسنون ؛ ظاهره يخرجُ القراءة، فإنّها مفروضة، فالمراد به المشروع، فيشمل الواجب والفرض والسنة ، أشار إليه البرجنديّ والقُهستاني في شرح النقاية»(۳). فإن قلت : يخرج عنه القومة ؛ لأنَّ فيهما ذكراً مسنوناً، وهو التحميد، والتسميع قلت : المراد بالذكر الذكر الطويل، وهذا ذكر قصير أشار إليه إلياس زاده في «شرح النقاية»(4).
[٤] قوله : ثمّ يثني ؛ أي يقرأ : سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك، وتبارك اسمك وتعالى
And between the takbirs of the two Eids, then he recites the thana'.
(And between the takbirs of the two Eids): so the conclusion is that every standing in which there is a prescribed remembrance, in it is placing (the hands), and every standing not like that, in it is releasing.
[4] (Then he recites thana')
And in summary: the placement of hands under the navel is not as those who think it has no reliable evidence suppose; indeed, it has been established from the Prophet (peace be upon him) placing the hands above the navel on the chest also in a narration of Ahmad and Ibn Khuzaymah, and al-Shafi‘i (may Allah be pleased with him) and his followers adopted it, and our companions (Hanafis) adopted it for women because placing the hands on the chest is more concealing for them, and for detail there is another place.
[1] The statement: 'And between the takbirs of the two Eids' i.e., the additional sunnah, and as for after them, in the first rak‘ah he places and recites after the three, and in the second rak‘ah when he finishes the additional (takbirs) and says takbir for bowing without placing, as stated in 'Majalis al-Abrar'.
(2) The statement: 'standing' i.e., actual or deemed, as when one prays sitting, as ‘Ali al-Qari said in 'Sharh al-Nuqayah'.
[3] The statement: 'prescribed' (masnun); apparently it excludes recitation (qira'ah), for it is obligatory; rather what is meant is 'prescribed' (mashru‘), including obligatory, fard, and sunnah, as al-Barjandi and al-Quhustani indicated in 'Sharh al-Nuqayah'. If you say: It excludes the qawma (rising) because in them there is a prescribed remembrance: tahmid and tasmi‘. I say: What is meant by dhikr is long dhikr, and this is short dhikr, as indicated by Ilyas Zadah in 'Sharh al-Nuqayah'.
[4] The statement: 'then he recites thana'' i.e., he recites: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika, wa tabaraka ismuka wa ta‘ala'
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with explanatory parsing. It discusses two matters: the general principle for hand placement and the recitation of thana'. The author first addresses the placement between the additional takbirs of Eid prayer, stating that hands are placed. Then he formulates a general rule: every standing that includes a sunnah dhikr (prescribed remembrance) requires placing hands, while standing without such dhikr (like the qawma after bowing) requires releasing them. He then discusses the recitation of thana' (Subhanaka Allahumma...). He clarifies that 'sunni' here means 'prescribed' (mashru‘), including wajib, fard, and sunnah, to address that recitation (qira'ah) is fard and not sunnah in the technical sense. He also addresses an objection regarding the qawma, explaining that the dhikr there (tahmid and tasmi‘) is short, so it does not qualify. Finally, he includes a summary on hand placement, mentioning that the Shafi‘i school places hands on the chest (based on other narrations) and that Hanafis adopt chest placement for women for modesty.

Key Terms
ثم يثني (thumma yuthannī): Then he recites the thana' (Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...).
قيام (qiyām): Standing position in prayer, whether actual or deemed (e.g., for those praying sitting).
ذكر مسنون (dhikr masnūn): Prescribed remembrance, including wajib, fard, and sunnah in the broad sense.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Only during qawma
C) Only during qunut
D) Never

Key Takeaway
Place hands during any standing that includes a prescribed lengthy dhikr, and release them during standings with short dhikr like the qawma.

Hand Placement in Prayer: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Explains the Hanafi ruling on hand placement and contrast with Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on hand placement for men and women and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Hand placement in prayer is sunnah: men below the navel, women on the chest – a distinction rooted in modesty.

The placement of hands during standing (qiyam) in prayer is a confirmed sunnah, but where exactly should they be placed? The Hanafi school distinguishes by gender: men place their hands below the navel, while women place them on the chest. This lesson explains the reasoning behind this differentiation and addresses the Shafi'i view that both men and women should place hands on the chest.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling for men and women regarding hand placement during qiyam.
Hanafi: men below navel, women on chest.
2
Identify the opposing school and their proof
State the Shafi'i position and the hadith they rely on (Prophet placing hands on chest).
Shafi'i: both men and women on chest, based on hadith from Ahmad and Ibn Khuzaymah.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response to the opponent's proof
Explain how the Hanafi school uses the same hadith but applies it to women only, due to modesty.
Hanafis accept the hadith but consider the chest placement more concealing for women.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference in prayer between the two schools.
Hanafi men place hands below navel; Shafi'i men and all women on chest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبين تكبيرات العيدين) ، فالحاصل أن كل قيام" فيه ذكر مسنون" ففيه الوضع، وكُل قيام ليس كذا ففيه الإرسال. [٤] (ثم يثني ) وبالجملة؛ فليس وضع اليدين تحت السرِّةِ كما يظنّه الظانون أنه ليس له دليل (۱) معتد به ، نعم قد ثبت عن النبي الا الله وضع اليدين فوق السرة عند الصدر (١) أيضاً في رواية أحمد وابن خزيمة، وبه أخذ الشافعي الله ومن تبعه، وأخذ به أصحابنا في حق النساء ؛ لأنَّ وضع اليدين على الصدر أستر لهنّ، وللتفصيل موضع آخر.
And between the takbirs of the two Eids, then he recites the thana'. So the conclusion is that every standing (qiyam) in which there is a supererogatory dhikr, there is placement (of hands); and every standing not like that, there is letting them hang. Then he recites thana'. In short: the placing of hands below the navel, as some people imagine, has no reliable evidence. Yes, it has been authentically reported from the Prophet (peace be upon him) placing hands above the navel upon the chest as well, in a narration of Ahmad and Ibn Khuzaymah, and Imam al-Shafi'i and his followers adopted it. Our companions adopted it for women, because placing hands on the chest is more concealing for them. And for more details, there is another place.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute. The author begins by stating the general principle: during any standing position in prayer that involves a supererogatory dhikr (like the opening supplication or recitation), the hands should be placed (usually under the navel for men). During other standings (e.g., between the two sajdahs without a long dhikr), hands should be left hanging. The author then addresses a common misconception that placing hands under the navel has no sound evidence. He clarifies that there is a hadith (from Ahmad and Ibn Khuzaymah) where the Prophet placed his hands on his chest. Imam al-Shafi'i adopted this as the general practice, whereas the Hanafi school uses it specifically for women, as it is more modest for them. For men, the Hanafi school maintains the position of placing hands under the navel, based on other evidences. This illustrates how the Hanafi school considers both modesty (sitr) and the general sunnah, differentiating between men and women.

Key Terms
وضع اليدين (wad' al-yadayn): Placement of the hands during standing in prayer, a sunnah act.
السرة (al-surrah): The navel; reference point for hand placement for men.
الإرسال (al-irsal): Letting the hands hang freely during qiyam when no supererogatory dhikr is performed.

Key Takeaway

Opening Supplication: Thana' vs. Tawajjuh
Intra-Hanafi dispute on opening supplication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on the opening supplication and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding tawajjuh.

Core Idea
After takbir, the relied-upon Hanafi position is to recite thana' only; tawajjuh is not part of the regular prayer.

When you begin prayer with the takbir, what do you say next? The Hanafi school has a clear position: the thana' (Subhanaka Allahumma) is recited. However, a difference exists within the school itself: Imam Abu Yusuf considered the tawajjuh (Inni wajjahtu) to be recommended. This lesson unpacks that dispute and explains the evidence behind each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and default ruling
After the opening takbir (tahrimah), there is a sunnah supplication. What does the matn state?
The matn says 'yuthni' (he recites thana') and 'la yuwajjihu' (he does not recite tawajjuh).
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Notice that the commentator specifies 'this is our position' (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) and then mentions Abu Yusuf's different view.
Abu Yusuf considers tawajjuh mustahabb, citing authentic hadiths.
3
Examine the proofs for each view
The passage lists hadith sources for thana' (with some weak chains) and for tawajjuh (authentic in Bukhari, Muslim). Compare the strength and relevance.
The Hanafi majority prioritizes the hadith of thana' as more specific to the opening.
4
Understand the tarjih mechanism
Why is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad relied upon over Abu Yusuf's? Consider the principle that the practice of the Companions and the established sunnah of the Prophet as understood by the majority of Hanafi imams carries weight.
The commentator refers to his larger work al-Si'ayah for further details.
5
Apply in practice
As a Hanafi, you recite thana' after takbir. If you follow Abu Yusuf's view, it is also acceptable but not the mufta bihi.
Knowing this difference prevents confusion in congregational prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٤] قوله : ثمّ يثني ؛ أي يقرأ : سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك، وتبارك اسمك وتعالى جدك، ولا إله غيرك ) ، وقد رويت قراءته عن النبي الله في «سنن أبي داود»، و«جامع الترمذي من حديث عائشةَ بسند ضعيف، وفي سنن ابن ماجة»، ومن حديث أبي سعيد عند النسائي والبيهقي، ومن حديث جابر عند البيهقي، وعن عمر بن الخطاب له في «صحيح مسلم»). [١]قوله : ولا يوجه ؛ أي لا يقرأ : «إني وجهت وجهي للذي فطر السماوات والارض حنيفاً ومـا أنـا من المشركين، إنّ صلاتي ونسكي ومحياي ومماتي لله ربّ العالمين، لا شريك له وبذلك أمرت وأنا أوّل المسلمين هذا عندنا، وأما عند أبي يوسف له تستحب قراءته ، كيف وقد ثبت ذلك عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في «صحيح البخاري» و«سنن ابن ماجه» و «سنن أبي داود»، و«جامع الترمذي وغيرها، وروى ، الجمع بين التوجيه والثناء (4) عند الطبراني والبيهقي وابن راهويه كما بسطنا ذلك في «السعاية»). [٢] قوله : بعد التحريمة ؛ وأمّا قبل التحريمة فاختار المتأخرون أن يقرأ : «إنى
[4] His saying: 'Then he recites thana'' meaning he recites: 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika, wa tabarakasmuka wa ta'ala jadduka, wa la ilaha ghayruka.' It has been narrated from the Prophet in Sunan Abi Dawud, Jami' al-Tirmidhi from Aisha with a weak chain, in Sunan Ibn Majah, from Abu Sa'id at Nasa'i and Bayhaqi, from Jabir at Bayhaqi, and from Umar ibn al-Khattab in Sahih Muslim. [1] His saying: 'And he does not recite tawajjuh' meaning he does not recite: 'Inni wajjahtu wajhiya lilladhi fatara al-samawati wal-arda hanifan wa ma ana min al-mushrikin, inna salati wa nusuki wa mahyaya wa mamati lillahi rabbil 'alamin, la sharika lahu wa bidhalika umirtu wa ana awwal al-muslimin.' This is our position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). As for Abu Yusuf, he considers it recommended to recite it, especially since it is established from the Messenger of Allah in Sahih al-Bukhari, Sunan Ibn Majah, Sunan Abi Dawud, Jami' al-Tirmidhi and others. And a narration combining tawajjuh and thana' is reported by Tabarani, Bayhaqi, and Ibn Rahawayh, as we have expanded in al-Si'ayah. [2] His saying: 'After the takbir' - as for before the takbir, the later scholars choose to recite 'Inni...'
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage covers an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the opening supplication in prayer. The matn states that after the takbir, the worshipper recites the thana' (Subhanaka Allahumma...) and does not recite the tawajjuh (Inni wajjahtu...). The commentator explains that this is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. However, Imam Abu Yusuf holds that reciting the tawajjuh is mustahabb (recommended), citing its strong authentication in several hadith collections. The commentator also notes that some narrations combine both thana' and tawajjuh, and he refers to his larger work al-Si'ayah for details. Additionally, the text clarifies that the issue is specifically about recitation after the takbir (takbir tahrimah); before the takbir, later scholars recommend reciting the tawajjuh. This shows the nuanced positions within the Hanafi school regarding which supplication to use and the weight of different hadith evidences.

Key Terms
الثناء (al-thana'): The opening supplication 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...' recited after takbir.
التوجيه (al-tawajjuh): The supplication 'Inni wajjahtu wajhiya...' recited after takbir.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that enters one into prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Tawajjuh (Inni wajjahtu)
C) Both thana' and tawajjuh
D) No supplication

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is to recite thana' (Subhanaka Allahumma) after takbir, not tawajjuh, but Abu Yusuf's view shows an internal difference.

Ruling on Reciting Tawajjuh After Takbir Tahrimah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on reciting tawajjuh after takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding recitation of tawajjuh after takbir tahrimah and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, tawajjuh is not recited; only thana' is recited after takbir.

After the takbir that starts prayer, a worshipper recites a short supplication. The Hanafi school has a nuanced position on which supplication to recite. This lesson examines the matn 'ولا يوجه' and its commentary, which establish that only thana' (سبحانك اللهم) is recited, not tawajjuh (إني وجهت وجهي), and explores the internal disagreement with Imam Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position according to the matn
Identify what the matn 'ولا يوجه' means and who it represents.
The matn reflects Abu Hanifa's position.
2
Identify the opposing view and its basis
Recognize that Imam Abu Yusuf differs and why he holds that tawajjuh is recommended.
Abu Yusuf relies on authentic hadiths in Sahih al-Bukhari and others.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the hadiths cited by Abu Yusuf that show the Prophet reciting tawajjuh.
These hadiths are considered authentic by all scholars.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand how Abu Hanifa's position addresses those authentic hadiths, interpreting them as optional or part of thana'.
The weak hadith of Aisha and Companion practice are given greater weight.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
Note the practical difference and which view is relied upon for fatwa.
The commentator says 'هذا عندنا' indicating the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يوجه) أراد بالثناء سبحانك الله ... إلى آخره، والتوجيه قراءة : «إِنِّي وَجْهَتُ وَجْهِيَ  ِللَّذِي فَطَرَ السَّمَوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ حَنِيفَاً ، وَمَا أَنَا مِنَ الْمُشْرِكِين» بعد التحريمة، وقد رويت قراءته عن النبي الله في «سنن أبي داود»، و«جامع الترمذي من حديث عائشةَ بسند ضعيف، وفي سنن ابن ماجة»، ومن حديث أبي سعيد عند النسائي والبيهقي، ومن حديث جابر عند البيهقي، وعن عمر بن الخطاب له في «صحيح مسلم»). قوله : ولا يوجه ؛ أي لا يقرأ : «إني وجهت وجهي للذي فطر السماوات والارض حنيفاً ومـا أنـا من المشركين، إنّ صلاتي ونسكي ومحياي ومماتي لله ربّ العالمين، لا شريك له وبذلك أمرت وأنا أوّل المسلمين هذا عندنا، وأما عند أبي يوسف له تستحب قراءته ، كيف وقد ثبت ذلك عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في «صحيح البخاري» و«سنن ابن ماجه» و «سنن أبي داود»، و«جامع الترمذي وغيرها، وروى الجمع بين التوجيه والثناء عند الطبراني والبيهقي وابن راهويه كما بسطنا ذلك في «السعاية»).
('And he does not recite tawajjuh') He meant by thana' 'Subhanaka Allahumma...' etc., and tawajjuh is reciting: 'Indeed I have turned my face toward He who created the heavens and the earth, inclining toward truth, and I am not of the polytheists' after the takbir tahrimah. And its recitation has been narrated from the Prophet ﷺ in Sunan Abi Dawud, Jami' al-Tirmidhi from the hadith of Aisha with a weak chain, and in Sunan Ibn Majah, and from the hadith of Abu Sa'id (at al-Nasa'i and al-Bayhaqi), and from the hadith of Jabir (at al-Bayhaqi), and from Umar ibn al-Khattab in Sahih Muslim. His statement: 'And he does not recite tawajjuh' meaning: he does not recite 'Inni wajjahtu wajhiya...' This is our (Hanafi) position. As for Abu Yusuf ﷺ, he holds that its recitation is recommended, because it is established from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ in Sahih al-Bukhari, Sunan Ibn Majah, Sunan Abi Dawud, Jami' al-Tirmidhi, and others, and the combination of tawajjuh and thana' has been narrated (by al-Tabarani, al-Bayhaqi, and Ibn Rahawayh) as we have detailed in al-Si'ayah.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the recitation of the opening supplication (tawajjuh) after the takbir tahrimah. The base text (matn) states 'ولا يوجه' meaning the worshipper does not recite tawajjuh. The commentator explains that this is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa: one recites thana' (سبحانك اللهم) and no tawajjuh. He cites that the hadith of Aisha in Sunan Abi Dawud and Tirmidhi is weak, and that the stronger evidence supports Abu Hanifa's view. However, Imam Abu Yusuf considers tawajjuh recommended (mustahabb) because it is authentically reported in Sahih al-Bukhari, among others. Some narrations combine tawajjuh and thana'. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa: only thana' is recited, not tawajjuh. The commentator notes that this is 'at our place' (عندنا), contrasting with Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
التوجيه (al-tawajjuh): The opening supplication beginning with 'إني وجهت وجهي' after the takbir.
الثناء (al-thana'): The supplication 'سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك' recited after takbir.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that commences the prayer.

C) Both
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is to recite only thana' after takbir, not tawajjuh, due to the weight of evidence.

Ta'awwudh is for Recitation, Not for Thana'
Ruling with proof: ta'awwudh tied to recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when ta'awwudh is recited in prayer and distinguish between the positions of Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Ta'awwudh follows recitation, so the masbuq recites it; the mu'tamm does not.

The source passage establishes that seeking refuge (ta'awwudh) before Qur'an recitation is sunnah, but its placement differs depending on one's role in congregational prayer. The text presents an intra-Hanafi debate: is ta'awwudh tied to recitation or to the opening praise (thana')? The preferred view ties it to recitation, leading to different practices for the latecomer and the follower.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Ta'awwudh is sunnah mu'akkadah before recitation; its omission does not invalidate prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The Quranic verse 16:98 commands seeking refuge when reciting the Qur'an, not when praising.
Surah an-Nahl:98
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'fa-sta'idh' is connected to the condition 'idha qara'ta al-Qur'an', indicating ta'awwudh is tied to qira'ah.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf held ta'awwudh is for thana'; Imam Muhammad and Abu Hanifa held it is for recitation. The mufta bihi is the latter, supported by the Quran.
Ali al-Qari refutes Abu Yusuf's view as contradicting the apparent meaning of the Quran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويتعود للقراءة، لا للثناء) المختار أن التّعودُ تبع للقراءة لا تبع للثناء ، فيقولُه المسبوق لا المؤتم) بناءً على أنَّ المسبوق يقرأ ولا يثني فيتعوذ ، والمؤتم يثني ولا يقرأ، فلا يتعوذ، وأمَّا مَن جعله تبعاً للثناء، فالحكم . عنده على عكس ما ذَكَرَه . ( ويؤخر عن تكبيرات العيدين) ؛ لأن التكبيرات بعد الثَّناء ، فينبغي أن يكون التَّعود متصلاً بالقراءة لا بالثناء. قوله : المختار ...الخ ؛ هذا هو قول محمد له ، وقال أبو يوسف له : هو تبع للثناء، قال في «الخلاصة»: هو الأصح ، وردَّه علي القاري له في «شرح النقاية» بأنه كيف يكون أصح وهو مخالف لظاهر القرآن، يعني قوله : فَإذا قرأت القُرْآنَ فَاسْتَعِدُ بِاللَّهِ مِنَ الشَّيْطَانِ الرَّحِيمِ ) (٢).
('And he seeks refuge for recitation, not for thana') The preferred opinion is that ta'awwudh follows recitation, not thana'. So the latecomer (masbuq) says it, not the follower (mu'tamm), because the latecomer recites and does not recite thana', so he seeks refuge. The follower recites thana' and does not recite, so he does not seek refuge. As for one who makes it follow thana', the ruling with him is the opposite of what he mentioned. ('And he delays it from the Eid takbirs') because the takbirs are after thana', so it is appropriate that ta'awwudh be connected to recitation, not to thana'. His statement: 'The preferred opinion...' This is the saying of Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: it is a follower of thana'. He said in al-Khulasa: it is the more correct. Ali al-Qari refuted it in Sharh al-Niqayah saying: how can it be more correct while it contradicts the apparent meaning of the Qur'an, namely His statement: 'So when you recite the Qur'an, seek refuge with Allah from the accursed Satan' (16:98).
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the timing and context of seeking refuge (ta'awwudh) in prayer. The base text states that ta'awwudh is for recitation, not for thana'. The commentator clarifies that the preferred opinion (mukhtar) is that ta'awwudh follows recitation. Consequently, a latecomer (masbuq) who catches up with the imam but needs to complete his own recitation recites ta'awwudh, while the follower (mu'tamm) who listens to the imam does not recite any ta'awwudh because he does not recite. The passage also addresses the delay of ta'awwudh from the Eid takbirs since the takbirs come after thana' and ta'awwudh should be connected to recitation. An intra-Hanafi dispute is mentioned: Imam Muhammad holds that ta'awwudh is for recitation, while Abu Yusuf holds it is for thana'. The commentator notes that al-Khulasa declares Abu Yusuf's view as 'asahh' (more correct), but Ali al-Qari refutes this by citing the Quranic verse (16:98) that explicitly connects seeking refuge with reciting the Quran, not with praise. The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is that of Imam Muhammad and Abu Hanifa: ta'awwudh is for recitation, so the masbuq recites it, the mu'tamm does not.

Key Terms
التعوذ (al-ta'awwudh): The act of saying 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim' before recitation.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A person who joins the congregational prayer late and misses one or more rak'ahs.
المؤتم (al-mu'tamm): A follower in congregational prayer who is not the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Ta'awwudh is sunnah tied to recitation, so the masbuq recites it, the mu'tamm does not.

Reciting Basmalah in Each Rak'ah: The Hanafi Dispute and Relied-Upon Position
Explains the varying positions on when to recite basmalah in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi transmissions regarding basmalah in prayer and explain why the Sahibayn's position is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Basmalah is sunnah in every rak'ah — Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's view is the correct and chosen position.

This passage addresses a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute: should the basmalah be recited in every rak'ah of prayer, or only in the first? While all agree it is sunnah in the first, the later rak'ahs are contested. We will examine the two transmissions and understand why the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad prevails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its agreed ruling
The act is reciting basmalah at the beginning of recitation after ta'awwudh. All agree it is sunnah in the first rak'ah.
2
Locate the point of ikhtilaf
The disagreement concerns the remaining rak'ahs (second, third, fourth). Should basmalah be recited there too?
3
State the transmission from Abu Hanifa
Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated that Abu Hanifa only recites basmalah in the first rak'ah, not in the others.
This transmission is from the nawadir (rare reports).
4
State the transmission of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that basmalah is recited in every rak'ah, while ta'awwudh is only in the first.
This is the position of the majority of the Hanafi school.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later authoritative works (Mukhtarat al-Nawazil, al-Qunyah, Fath al-Qadir) declare the Sahibayn's view as sahih al-mukhtar (correct and chosen). Thus, the operative ruling for fatwa is to recite basmalah in every rak'ah.
The commentary refers to a treatise for further detail.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ويسمى) أي يقرأ : بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم» عند ابتداء القراءة بعد التعوذ، وهذا في الركعة الأولى سنة اتفاقي، وفي باقي الركعاتِ اختلافي، فروى الحسنُ عن أبي حنيفة له أنه لا يأتي بهما إلا في الأولى. وروى أبو يوسف أنه يأتي بها في كلّ ركعة والتعوّذ في الأولى فقط، وهذا هو قولهما، وهذا هو الصحيح المختار ، كما في «مختارات النوازل» و«القنية» و«فتح القدير وغيرها، وتفصيل هذا ليطلب من رسالتي «إحكام القنطرة في أحكام البسملة).
('And he recites the basmalah') i.e., he recites 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' at the beginning of recitation after ta'awwudh. This is agreed upon as sunnah in the first rak'ah, but there is difference regarding the remaining rak'ahs. Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he does not recite it except in the first. Abu Yusuf narrated that he recites it in every rak'ah, but ta'awwudh only in the first. This is their saying, and this is the correct and chosen (view), as in Mukhtarat al-Nawazil, al-Qunyah, Fath al-Qadir, and others. The detail of this is to be sought in my treatise 'Ihkam al-Qantarah fi Ahkam al-Basmalah'.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the recitation of basmalah in prayer. The base text 'ويسمي' indicates that the worshipper recites the basmalah at the start of recitation after seeking refuge. The commentator explains that there is agreement (ittifaqi) that reciting basmalah in the first rak'ah is sunnah. However, there is a difference (ikhtilafi) regarding the other rak'ahs. One transmission from Abu Hanifa, via al-Hasan ibn Ziyad, states that he only recites basmalah in the first rak'ah. Another transmission from Abu Yusuf states that he recites basmalah in every rak'ah, but ta'awwudh only in the first. The commentary declares that the view of Abu Yusuf (and Muhammad) is the correct and chosen (sahih al-mukhtar) position, as supported by later works. The commentator refers to his own treatise for further details. Thus, the mufta bihi is that basmalah is recited in every rak'ah silently.

Key Terms
البسملة (al-basmalah): The phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' recited before the Fatiha.
السنة (al-sunnah): The recommended act; in this context, basmalah is sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only in the first rak'ah
B) In every rak'ah
C) Only in audible prayers
D) It is not recited at all

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that basmalah is recited silently in every rak'ah of prayer.

Ta'awwudh Follows Recitation: Ruling for Masbuq and Mu'tam
Ruling with proof on ta'awwudh timing and masbuq/mu'tam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on who says ta'awwudh in congregational prayer (masbuq vs mu'tam) and justify it with the Quranic evidence and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Ta'awwudh is tied to recitation: the masbuq recites and says it; the mu'tam does not recite and does not say it.

This passage from a sharh of al-Wiqayah clarifies two points: the position of ta'awwudh in the prayer sequence and who among the followers recites it. The chosen Hanafi view, based on the Quran, links ta'awwudh to recitation. Understanding this affects both the masbuq (latecomer) and the mu'tam (full-time follower), as well as the placement of ta'awwudh in Eid prayer after the extra takbirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of followers
Distinguish between masbuq (joins late, completes missed rak'ahs) and mu'tam (prays from beginning). The masbuq recites in his qada', while the mu'tam does not recite behind the imam.
This recitation difference is key to the ruling.
2
State the chosen position (mukhtar)
The chosen Hanafi view is that ta'awwudh follows recitation, not thana'. Therefore, the masbuq says it, and the mu'tam does not.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Verse 16:98 commands seeking refuge when reciting. This directly links ta'awwudh to the act of recitation.
The dalil is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalala, leaving room for interpretation.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf held that ta'awwudh follows thana'. Under his view, the mu'tam would say ta'awwudh and the masbuq would not. Understand the practical difference.
Ali al-Qari refuted Abu Yusuf's view as contradictory to the Quran.
5
Apply to Eid prayer timing
In Eid prayer, the extra takbirs come after thana'. Since ta'awwudh follows recitation, it is delayed until after the takbirs to maintain connection with the recitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيقولُهُ المسبوق لا المؤتم ويؤخِّرُ عن تكبيرات العيدين

المختار أن التّعودُ تبع للقراءة لا تبع للثناء ، فيقولُه المسبوق لا المؤتم) بناءً على أنَّ المسبوق يقرأ ولا يثني فيتعوذ ، والمؤتم يثني ولا يقرأ، فلا يتعوذ، وأمَّا مَن جعله تبعاً للثناء، فالحكم . عنده على عكس ما ذَكَرَه . ( ويؤخر عن تكبيرات العيدين) ؛ لأن التكبيرات بعد الثَّناء ، فينبغي أن يكون التَّعود متصلاً بالقراءة لا بالثناء.

[1 ] قوله : المختار ...الخ ؛ هذا هو قول محمد له ، وقال أبو يوسف له : هو تبع للثناء، قال في «الخلاصة»: هو الأصح ، وردَّه علي القاري له في «شرح النقاية» بأنه كيف يكون أصح وهو مخالف لظاهر القرآن، يعني قوله : فَإذا قرأت القُرْآنَ فَاسْتَعِدُ بِاللَّهِ مِنَ الشَّيْطَانِ الرَّحِيمِ ).
The masbuq says it, not the mu'tam, and he delays it after the Eid takbirs. The chosen position is that ta'awwudh follows recitation, not thana'. So the masbuq says it because he recites and does not say thana'; the mu'tam says thana' and does not recite, so he does not say ta'awwudh. As for the one who makes it follow thana', the ruling with him is the opposite of what was mentioned. And he delays it after the Eid takbirs because the takbirs come after thana', so ta'awwudh should be connected to recitation, not thana'. [Footnote 1] He said: 'The chosen...etc.' This is the statement of Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said it is following thana'. In al-Khulasa it is said it is the most correct. Ali al-Qari rejected this in Sharh al-Niqaya saying how can it be most correct while it contradicts the apparent meaning of the Quran, meaning His statement: 'When you recite the Quran, seek refuge with Allah from the accursed Shaytan.'
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the sharh of al-Wiqaya. It discusses two issues: first, who says the ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) in prayer. According to the chosen position of the school, ta'awwudh is tied to recitation, not to the thana' (opening praise). Therefore, the masbuq (latecomer) who recites in the remaining part of the prayer says the ta'awwudh, while the mu'tam (follower) who only says the thana' and does not recite does not say it. Abu Yusuf held that ta'awwudh follows thana', which would reverse the ruling. However, the preferred view is that of Imam Muhammad, supported by the Quranic verse (16:98) commanding isti'adha when reciting. Second, the ta'awwudh is delayed until after the Eid takbirs because the takbirs come after thana', and the ta'awwudh should be directly before recitation, not interrupted by thana'. The footnote mentions the ikhtilaf between Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, with the majority favoring Muhammad, and a refutation of Abu Yusuf's position based on the Quranic command.

Key Terms
التعوذ (al-ta'awwudh): Seeking refuge in Allah from Shaytan by saying 'A'udhu billahi min al-shaytan al-rajim' before recitation.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A latecomer in congregational prayer who joins the imam after the first rak'ah and completes the missed rak'ahs after the imam's salam.
المؤتم (al-mu'tam): The follower who prays behind an imam from the beginning of the prayer.
الثناء (al-thana'): The opening praise recited after the first takbir, e.g., 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika...'
تكبيرات العيدين (takbirat al-'idayn): The additional takbirs recited in the Eid prayer, which come after thana' and before ta'awwudh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen Hanafi position, why does the masbuq say ta'awwudh while the mu'tam does not?
A) Because the masbuq raises his hands for qunut.
B) Because ta'awwudh follows recitation, and the masbuq recites in his qada'.
C) Because the mu'tam is not required to recite any supplications.
D) Because the masbuq has a higher reward.

Key Takeaway
The masbuq says ta'awwudh because it follows recitation; the mu'tam does not because he does not recite behind the imam.

Ruling on Saying Bismillah in Prayer: Hanafi Position and Dispute with Shafi'i
Detailing the ruling of tasmiyah, its placement, and the ikhtilaf on whether it is an ayah of al-Fatihah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on where and how to recite the basmalah in prayer and explain why the Shafi'i school differs.

Core Idea
In Hanafi prayer, basmalah is recited silently at the start of al-Fatihah in every rak'ah — it is sunnah, not an ayah.

Reciting 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' in prayer is a practice with differing views on its status and method. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling: where to recite it, whether aloud or silently, and how it differs from the Shafi'i position. We will trace the proof from the practice of the Companions and understand the intra-Hanafi nuances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is saying the basmalah (tasmiyah) at the beginning of recitation in prayer. In the Hanafi school, it is sunnah, not fard or wajib. Determine this from the passage: it is 'sunnah' by agreement in the first rak'ah.
The passage says 'sunnah اتفاقي' showing consensus on its sunnah status in the first rak'ah.
2
Locate the dalil
The main proof cited is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'The Messenger of Allah, Abu Bakr, and Umar did not recite Bismillah aloud in any obligatory prayer.' This is a ahad hadith, and its transmission is zanni but its indication (dalala) is qati' (clear) for silent recitation.
The dalil is quoted in the Arabic: 'ما جهر رسول الله...'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly negates jahr (audible recitation) of the basmalah in obligatory prayers. Since the Prophet and the caliphs did not recite it aloud, the Hanafi school concludes it must be recited silently. This is the wajh al-dalalah: absence of jahr implies israr (silence).
This is a dalil naqli (textual evidence).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that basmalah is an ayah of al-Fatihah and thus must be recited aloud in audible prayers. They rely on other narrations that show the Prophet reciting it aloud. The Hanafi response is that those narrations are weak and contradict the established practice of the Companions.
The passage mentions three opinions on whether basmalah is an ayah.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Among the Hanafi imams, the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that basmalah is recited in every rak'ah at the beginning of al-Fatihah only, not between al-Fatihah and the surah, and it is recited silently. This is supported by Mukhtarat al-Nawazil, al-Qunyah, and Fath al-Qadir.
The intra-Hanafi differences: Abu Hanifa (in one narration) said only in first rak'ah; Abu Yusuf said in every rak'ah; Muhammad said at beginning of each surah. The mufta bihi follows Abu Yusuf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسمي لا بين الفاتحة والسورة ويسرهن

قوله : ويسمي ; أي يقرأ : بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم عند ابتداء القراءة بعد التعوذ، وهذا في الركعة الأولى سنة اتفاقي، وفي باقي الركعاتِ اختلافي، فروى الحسنُ عن أبي حنيفة أنه لا يأتي بهما إلا في الأولى. وروى أبو يوسف أنه يأتي بها في كلّ ركعة والتعوّذ في الأولى فقط، وهذا هو قولهما، وهذا هو الصحيح المختار ، كما في «مختارات النوازل» و«القنية» و«فتح القدير وغيرها، وتفصيل هذا ليطلب من رسالتي «إحكام القنطرة في أحكام البسملة).

قوله : لا بين الفاتحة والسورة ; أي لا يقرأ بسم الله في أول السورة، بل في أوّل الفاتحة فقط، هذا هو المشهور من مذهب أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ، وعند محمد يأتي بها في أول السورة أيضاً، والخلاف في الاستنان، أما عدم الكراهة فمتفق عليه ; ولهذا صرّح في «الذخيرة» و«المجتبى» بأنه لو سمى بين الفاتحة والسورة كان حسناً عند أبي حنيفة به سواء كانت السورة مقروءة جهراً أو سراً، ورجحه ابنُ الهمام وابنُ أمير حاج. كذا في «البحر الرائق» و«منح الغفار».

قوله : ويسرهن ; أي يخفي الثناء والتعوذ والتسمية خلافاً للشافعي في التسمية بناء على أنه آية من الفاتحة عنده. لما أخرجه ابن أبي شيبة عن ابن مسعود : «أنه كان يخفي ببسم الله الرحمن الرحيم والاستعاذة، وربنا لك الحمد»، وأخرج أبو بكر الرازي في كتاب «أحكام القرآن» عنه قال : «ما جهر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في صلاة مكتوبة ببسم الله ، ولا أبو بكر ولا عمر، وفي الباب أخبار كثيرة بسطناها مع ذكر الأخبار الدالة على جهر التسمية مع ما لها وما عليها في «إحكام القنطرة في أحكام البسملة» فلتطالع.

وقد اختلف في هذا الباب على أقوال : أحدها : أنها آية من الفاتحة ومن كل سورة. وثانيها : أنها ليست بآية مطلقاً، وهو مختارُ مالك والمشهور من مذهب الشافعي، هو الأول. وثالثها: أنها آية من الفاتحة فقط، وهو مختار بعض الشافعية.
And he says the basmalah, not between al-Fatihah and the surah, and he recites them silently. [Commentary:] He said: 'And he says the basmalah' i.e., he recites 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' at the beginning of recitation after ta'awwudh. This is sunnah in the first rak'ah by agreement, and in the remaining rak'ahs there is ikhtilaf. Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he does not recite them except in the first. Abu Yusuf narrated that he recites it in every rak'ah and ta'awwudh only in the first. This is their statement and it is the correct chosen view, as in Mukhtarat al-Nawazil, al-Qunyah, Fath al-Qadir, etc. Details are to be sought from my treatise 'Ihkam al-Qantarah fi Ahkam al-Basmalah'. He said: 'Not between al-Fatihah and the surah' i.e., he does not recite Bismillah at the beginning of the surah, but only at the beginning of al-Fatihah. This is the well-known (mashhur) view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad, he recites it at the beginning of the surah as well. The ikhtilaf is in terms of istihbab (recommendation); as for the absence of karahah (dislike), there is agreement. Hence it is stated in al-Dhakhirah and al-Mujtaba that if one recites the basmalah between al-Fatihah and the surah, it is good (hasan) according to Abu Hanifa, whether the surah is recited aloud or silently. Ibn al-Humam and Ibn Amir Hajj preferred this. Likewise in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and Minah al-Ghaffar. He said: 'And he recites them silently' i.e., he conceals the thana', ta'awwudh, and tasmiyah, contrary to al-Shafi'i regarding the tasmiyah, based on his view that it is an ayah of al-Fatihah. This is based on what Ibn Abi Shayba narrated from Ibn Mas'ud: 'He used to conceal Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim, al-isti'adha, and Rabbana lakal-hamd.' And Abu Bakr al-Razi narrated in his book Ahkam al-Quran from him: 'The Messenger of Allah, Abu Bakr, and Umar did not recite Bismillah aloud in any obligatory prayer.' There are many hadiths on this, which we have detailed in 'Ihkam al-Qantarah'. And there is ikhtilaf on this issue: first opinion: it is an ayah of al-Fatihah and of every surah. Second: it is not an ayah at all—this is the choice of Malik, and the well-known view of al-Shafi'i is the first. Third: it is an ayah of al-Fatihah only—this is the choice of some Shafi'is.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of al-Wiqaya discusses the ruling of saying Bismillah in prayer. It covers three sub-issues: (1) In which rak'ah is the basmalah recited? It is sunnah in the first rak'ah by agreement, but there is ikhtilaf for subsequent rak'ahs. The correct view is that it is recited in every rak'ah, but ta'awwudh only in the first. (2) The basmalah is recited only at the beginning of al-Fatihah, not between al-Fatihah and the surah. However, if one does recite it there, it is not disliked. Imam Muhammad held that it is recited at the beginning of the surah as well, but the mashhur view is that it is only at al-Fatihah. (3) The basmalah and ta'awwudh are recited silently. This is proven by the practice of Ibn Mas'ud and the early caliphs. This is contrary to al-Shafi'i, who holds that the basmalah is an ayah of al-Fatihah and thus must be recited aloud. The passage also summarizes three opinions on whether basmalah is an ayah: (a) it is an ayah of al-Fatihah and every surah (Shafi'i's well-known view), (b) it is not an ayah at all (Maliki), (c) it is an ayah of al-Fatihah only (some Shafi'is). The Hanafi position is that it is not an ayah of al-Fatihah, and therefore it is recited silently.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): Saying 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' at the beginning of recitation in prayer.
البسملة (al-basmalah): Same as tasmiyah; the phrase 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim'.
الفاتحة (al-fatihah): The opening chapter of the Quran, recited in every rak'ah of prayer.
السورة (al-surah): A chapter of the Quran; here refers to the surah recited after al-Fatihah in prayer.
الإخفاء (al-ikhfa'): Silent recitation, i.e., moving the lips without audible sound.
الجهر (al-jahr): Audible recitation.
الآية (al-ayah): A verse of the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) At the beginning of every surah recited in prayer
B) Only at the beginning of al-Fatihah in the first rak'ah
C) At the beginning of al-Fatihah in every rak'ah
D) Between al-Fatihah and the surah in every rak'ah

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the basmalah is a sunnah recited silently at the start of al-Fatihah in every rak'ah; it is not an ayah of al-Fatihah, contrary to the Shafi'i position.

The Basmalah in Prayer: Hanafi and Shafi‘i Dispute
Refuting Shafi‘i view on basmalah with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the basmalah in prayer, identify the key hadith evidence, and evaluate the Hanafi response to the Shafi‘i interpretation.

Core Idea
The basmalah is recited silently in prayer because the Prophet and caliphs did not recite it aloud.

The basmalah—saying 'Bismillahir Rahmanir Rahim'—is a point of contention between the Hanafi and Shafi‘i schools. While both agree it is recited, the Hanafis maintain it is not part of Surah al-Fatihah and should be recited silently. This lesson examines the evidence, particularly the hadith of Anas, and the Hanafi refutation of the Shafi‘i reading.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core question
What exactly is disputed about the basmalah? The two main issues are: (1) whether it is a verse of al-Fatihah, and (2) whether it is recited aloud or silently.
2
State the Hanafi position and its evolution
The early Hanafis (qudamā') held the basmalah is completely outside the Quran. The later Hanafis (mutā'akhirīn) held it is a verse of the Quran but not part of any surah, which is the relied-upon view.
This later view is the basis for the Tarawih ruling: the imam must recite basmalah aloud at the start of each surah to ensure completeness.
3
Analyze the key hadith evidence
The hadith from Anas (narrated by Muslim, Bukhari, and others) states that the Prophet and the caliphs opened recitation with 'Al-ḥamdu lillāhi rabbil-‘ālamīn'. Variant narrations explicitly mention that they recited the basmalah silently.
The silence of the narrators about reciting it aloud is evidence of silent recitation.
4
Examine the Shafi‘i interpretation and the Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi‘i interprets the hadith to mean they began with the surah, not that the basmalah was omitted. Al-Zayla‘i refutes this by arguing that interpreting the hadith as merely stating the beginning of the surah is pointless because it is obvious; rather, the clear meaning is that the basmalah was not recited aloud.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Hanafis recite the basmalah silently in all prayers; Shafi‘is recite it aloud in audible prayers. This affects congregational prayer, especially when followers belong to different schools.
The Tarawih ruler also differs: Hanafi imams must recite basmalah aloud to complete the Quran fully.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة صفة الصلاة

[۲] لا عندنا ، وكثير من الأحاديث الصحاح وارد في أنه " والخلفاء الراشدين ورابعها : إنّها آية فذة من القرآن، لكن ليست من الفاتحة ولا من غيرها، وهو مختار متأخري الحنفية، والأصح عندهم.
وخامسها : أنها بعض آية من السور كلهما.
وسادسها : أنها آية من الفاتحة، وجزء آية من غيرها.
وسابعها : عكسه.
وثامنها : أنها بعض آية من الفاتحة فقط.

[٤] قوله : في أنه ... الخ ؛ فعند مسلم عن أنس: «صلیت وراء رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأبي بكر وعمر و عثمان فكانوا يستفتحون القراءة بـ الحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ»، وكذا رواه البخاري.
وفي رواية النسائي وأحمد وابن حبان : «كانوا يجهرون بـ الحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ»، وفي رواية الطبراني وابن خزيمة وأبي نعيم والطحاوي: «فكانوا يسرون ببسم الله»، وفي الباب أخبار أخر صحيحة بسطها الزيلعي في نصب الراية، وذكرتها في «إحكام القنطرة».

[٥] قوله : يفتتحون ... الخ ؛ قال الترمذي في «جامعه»: «العمل على هذا عند أهل العلم من أصحاب رسول الله ، والتابعين ومن بعدهم أنهم كانوا يستفتحون القراءة بـ : بـ الحَمدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ .
وقال الشافعي رحمه الله : إنما معنى الحديث أنهم كانوا يفتتحون القراءة بالحمدِ معناه أنهم كانوا يبدأون بفاتحة الكتاب قبل السورة ، وليس معناه أنهم كانوا لا يقرؤنَ بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم، وكان الشافعي رحمه الله يرى أن يبدأ ببسم الله، وأن يجهر بها إذا جهر بالقراءة». انتهى
وقال الزيلعي في «تخريج أحاديث الهداية»: «حمل الافتتاح بـ الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ على السورةِ لا الآية مما يستبعده القريحة، وتمجه الأفهام الصحيحة ؛ لأنَّ هذا من العلم الذي يعرفه العام والخاص، كما يعلمون أن الفجر ركعتان والظهر أربع، فليس في نقل مثل هذا فائدة.
فكيف يظن أن أنساً به قصد تعريفهم بهذا ، وإنما مثل هذا مثل أن يقول : فكانوا يركعون قبل السجود، أو فكانوا يجهرون في العشاء والفجر، وأيضاً فلو أريد به سورة الحمد لقيل : كانوا يفتتحونَ بأم القرآن أو بفاتحة الكتاب، أو بسورة الحمد، هذا هو المعروف في تسميتها عندهم.
Book of Prayer – Description of Prayer

[2] Not according to us. And many authentic hadiths have come regarding that – and the four Rightly Guided Caliphs. And the fourth (view): It is a single verse from the Quran, but not from al-Fatihah nor from other (surahs). This is the chosen view of the later Hanafis, and the most correct according to them.
And the fifth: That it is part of a verse from the surahs, from both.
And the sixth: That it is a verse from al-Fatihah and part of a verse from other than it.
And the seventh: The opposite.
And the eighth: That it is only part of a verse from al-Fatihah.
And the ninth: That it is permissible to consider it a verse from the surahs, and to consider it outside it based on the fact that it was revealed once and not revealed another time. This is what al-Suyuti approved in his Hashiyat Tafsir al-Baydawi. And the refinement of these schools has been completed by us in Ihkam al-Qantara, so refer to it.

His saying: “Not according to us” – for our early scholars went to the view that it is completely outside the Quran, like Amin, after “nor of those who go astray”, for it is not a part of the Quran. And our later scholars went to the view that it is a verse of the Quran, but not from a surah, and this is stronger in consideration. And based on this they said: The imam of Tarawih who completes the Quran in it must recite it aloud at the beginning of a surah – whichever surah he wishes – so that the completion is not deficient.

His saying: “And many … etc.” – the purpose is to refute the Shafi‘is by proving the silent recitation of the basmalah and invalidating it being a verse of al-Fatihah.

His saying: “Regarding that … etc.” – For Muslim narrated from Anas: “I prayed behind the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman, and they used to open the recitation with ‘Al-ḥamdu lillāhi rabbil-‘ālamīn’.” And similarly al-Bukhari narrated it.
And in the narration of al-Nasa’i, Ahmad, and Ibn Hibban: “They used to recite aloud ‘Al-ḥamdu lillāhi rabbil-‘ālamīn’.” And in the narration of al-Tabarani, Ibn Khuzaymah, Abu Nu‘aym, and al-Tahawi: “They used to recite silently the Basmalah.” And there are other authentic hadiths on the topic, which al-Zayla‘i expanded in Nasb al-Rayah, and I mentioned them in Ihkam al-Qantara.

His saying: “They open … etc.” – al-Tirmidhi said in his Jami‘: “The practice according to the people of knowledge from the Companions of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, the Successors, and those after them is that they used to open the recitation with ‘Al-ḥamdu lillāhi rabbil-‘ālamīn’.”
And al-Shafi‘i (may Allah have mercy on him) said: “The meaning of the hadith is that they used to open the recitation with al-Hamd, meaning they used to begin with Surah al-Fatihah before a (other) surah, and it does not mean that they did not recite ‘Bismillahir Rahmanir Rahim’. And al-Shafi‘i (may Allah have mercy on him) held the view that one should begin with ‘Bismillah’ and that one should recite it aloud if one recites aloud.” End quote.
And al-Zayla‘i said in his Takhrij Ahadith al-Hidayah: “Interpreting the opening with ‘Al-ḥamdu lillāhi rabbil-‘ālamīn’ as pertaining to the surah and not the verse is something that the intellect rejects and sound minds abhor; because this is knowledge that the layman and the elite know, just as they know that Fajr is two rak‘ahs and Zuhr is four. There is no benefit in such transmission.
How could it be thought that Anas intended to inform them of this? Rather this is like saying: they used to bow before prostrating, or they used to recite aloud in ‘Isha’ and Fajr. Moreover, if the surah al-Hamd were intended, it would have been said: they used to open with Umm al-Qur’an or with al-Fatihah or with Surah al-Hamd. This is the well-known way of naming it among them.”
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute over the basmalah (Bismillah) in prayer, focusing on its status and recitation. The author enumerates nine different opinions (madhhabs) about the basmalah's relation to the Quran, but he quickly narrows down to the Hanafi view. According to the early Hanafi scholars, the basmalah is entirely outside the Quran, like the word 'Amin' after Surah al-Fatihah. However, the later Hanafis (mutā'akhirīn) adopted the position that it is indeed a verse of the Quran, but not part of any surah, and this is the stronger view in the school. Based on this, they rule that the imam leading Tarawih prayer who intends to complete a full recitation of the Quran must recite the basmalah aloud at the beginning of any surah he starts, to ensure completeness.

The author then uses hadith evidence to refute the Shafi‘i position. The key hadith from Anas states that the Prophet and the caliphs used to open recitation with 'Al-ḥamdu lillāhi rabbil-‘ālamīn', without mentioning the basmalah. The Shafi‘is interpret this to mean they began with the surah, not that they omitted the basmalah. But the author, quoting al-Zayla‘i, argues that such an interpretation is implausible because the Companions would not need to state something so obvious (that they started with the surah); rather, the clear meaning is that they did not recite the basmalah aloud. Hence, the Hanafi ruling that the basmalah is recited silently (isrār) in prayer is correct. The passage underscores the Hanafi reliance on istihsan and the practice of the early community to determine the ruling.

Key Terms
بسملة (basmalah): The phrase 'Bismillahir Rahmanir Rahim' said before reciting Quran.
الإسرار (al-isrār): Silent recitation, as opposed to jahr (audible recitation).
قدماء (qudamā'): Early Hanafi scholars, as opposed to mutā'akhirīn (later scholars).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi position (mutā'akhirīn), what is the status of the basmalah?
A) It is completely outside the Quran, like Amin.
B) It is a verse of the Quran, but not part of any surah.
C) It is a verse of al-Fatihah and recited aloud.
D) It is not recited in prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the basmalah is recited silently in prayer, based on the practice of the early community and the hadith of Anas, contrary to the Shafi‘i view.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Hanafi Position on Jahr Basmala and Surah Fatihah Naming
Refuting claims of jahr with Bismillah and clarifying surah naming

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on jahr basmala, explain the hadith evidence for silent recitation, and evaluate the opposing arguments.

Core Idea
The basmala is recited silently; jahr hadiths are weak and the Sahaba's practice is decisive.

The recitation of Bismillah aloud (jahr) in prayer is a point of dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is. This passage presents the Hanafi refutation by analyzing hadith chains and clarifying the early practice of the Sahaba. It also addresses the later naming of Surah Fatihah as 'Al-Hamd', distinguishing it from the actual recitation of the companions.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school holds the basmala should be recited silently in prayer. The passage argues jahr is not established from authentic hadith.
This is the central claim of the lesson.
2
Identify the opposing view and their proof
The opposing school (e.g., Shafi'is) cite hadiths from Al-Daraqutni, Al-Hakim, Al-Bayhaqi that the Prophet recited Bismillah aloud.
These are considered later collections with weaker chains.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof from Sahaba practice
Examine the hadith of Anas (from Sahih Muslim) describing Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman commencing prayer with 'Al-Hamdu Lillahi' without mentioning Bismillah. Note the explicit negation of any basmala recitation.
This is the primary dalil for the Hanafi position.
4
Critique the opposing proof by jarh (impugning narrators)
The passage asserts that every jahr hadith contains a liar, abandoned, or defective narrator. This is a methodological critique: weakness in transmission undermines the proof.
The Hanafi response relies on criteria of hadith authenticity (jarh wa ta'dil).
5
Conclude with thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical difference: Hanafis recite silently; Shafi'is recite aloud in audible prayers. The Hanafi view is preferred because the jahr hadiths are not sahih and the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs is relied upon.
Tarjih is based on strength of evidence, not mere preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما تسميتها بـ الحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ فلم تنقل عن رسول الله، ولا عن أصحابه، ولا عن التابعين ولا عن أحدٍ يحتج بقوله، وأما تسميتها بالحمد فعرف متأخر، يقال : فلان قرأ سورة الحمد وأين هذا من قوله : فكانوا يستفتحون بالحمد الله رب العالمين، فإنّ هذا لا يجوز أن يراد به السورة إلا بدليل صحيح.
فإن قيل : قد روى الوليد بن مسلم عن الأوزاعي عن اسحاق بن عبد الله بن أبي طلحة عن أنس : الاستفتاح بأم القرآن، وهذا يدل على أنه أراد السورة. قلنا : هذا مروي بالمعنى، والصحيح عن الأوزاعي ما رواه مسلم عن الوليد بن مسلم عنه عن قتادة عن أنس قال: صليت خلف أبي بكر وعمر وعثمان فكانوا يستفتحون بالحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ بَيْ العلمين، لا يذكرون بسم الله في أوّل قراءة ولا في آخرها.
ثم أخرجه مسلم عن الوليد عن الأوزاعي أخبرني اسحاق بن عبد الله بن أبي طلحة أنه سمع أنس بن مالك الله يذكر ذلك، هكذا رواه مسلم في صحيحه. عاطفاً له على حديث قتادة له، وهذا اللفظ المخرج في الصحيح هو الثابت عن الأوزاعي، واللفظ الآخر إن كان محفوظاً فهو مروي بالمعنى. انتهى كلام الزَّيْلَعِي
فإن قلت : يعارض هذا ما ثبت عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه كان يجهر ببسم الله، أخرجه الدارقطني والحاكم والبيهقي والخطيب البغدادي وغيرهم. قلت : ليس حديث من أحاديث الجهر سالماً عن الجرح فما من حديث منها إلا في سنده كذاب أو متروك أو مجروح، كما بسطه الزيلعي والحازمي وغيرهما، فلا تعارض الأحاديث الصحيحة.
ويؤيده أنه لم يرو أحاديث الجهر أحدٌ من أصحاب الكتب الستَّةِ وأصحاب المسانيد المعتبرة، ولم يخرجه إلا مثل الحاكم والخطيب والدارقطني والبيهقي الذين يجمعون الغرائب والمنكرات، بل وفي كتبهم أحاديث كثيرة موضوعة، مع أنه يحتمل أن يكون الجهر بالتسمية من النبي له في بعض الأحيان بياناً للجواز، أو جهر تعليماً، أو كان الجهر به اتفاقياً لا اختيارياً.
وعند أبي داود في كتاب «المراسيل» عن سعيد بن جبير ه قال : «كان رسول الله يجهر ببسم الله الرحمن الرحيم، وكان أهل مكة يدعون مسيلمة: الرحمن، فقالوا إنّ محمداً يدعو له اليمامة، فأمر الله رسوله فما جهر بهما حتى مات، وهذا يدل على أنّ الجهر منسوخ، وإن شئت تفصيلاً تاماً في هذا البحث، فارجع إلى رسالتي إحكام القنطرة
As for naming it 'Al-Hamdu Lillahi Rabbil Alameen', it has not been transmitted from the Messenger of Allah, nor from his companions, nor from the followers, nor from anyone whose statement is relied upon. As for naming it 'Al-Hamd', it is a later custom; it is said: so-and-so recited Surah Al-Hamd. Where is this from his statement: 'They used to commence with Al-Hamdu Lillahi Rabbil Alameen'? Indeed, this cannot be intended to mean the surah except with a valid proof. If it is said: Al-Walid ibn Muslim narrated from Al-Awzai from Ishaq ibn Abdullah ibn Abi Talha from Anas: 'The opening with Umm Al-Quran', and this indicates that he intended the surah. We say: This is narrated by meaning, and the correct from Al-Awzai is what Muslim narrated from Al-Walid ibn Muslim from him from Qatada from Anas who said: I prayed behind Abu Bakr, Umar, and Uthman, and they used to commence with 'Al-Hamdu Lillahi Rabbil Alameen', not mentioning Bismillah at the beginning of the recitation nor at the end. Then Muslim brought it out from Al-Walid from Al-Awzai: Ishaq ibn Abdullah ibn Abi Talha informed me that he heard Anas ibn Malik mention that. Thus Muslim narrated it in his Sahih, connecting it to the hadith of Qatada from him. And this wording brought out in the Sahih is the established one from Al-Awzai. The other wording, if preserved, is narrated by meaning. End of Zaylai's words. If you say: This is contradicted by what is established from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that he used to recite Bismillah aloud, reported by Al-Daraqutni, Al-Hakim, Al-Bayhaqi, Al-Khatib Al-Baghdadi, and others. I say: Not a single hadith of the jahr hadiths is free from defect; there is no hadith among them except that in its chain there is a liar, a deserted narrator, or a defective one, as expanded by Al-Zaylai, Al-Hazimi, and others. So they do not contradict the authentic hadiths. This is supported by the fact that none of the authors of the six books and authoritative musnads narrated the jahr hadiths; they are only reported by the likes of Al-Hakim, Al-Khatib, Al-Daraqutni, and Al-Bayhaqi, who collect strange and objectionable hadiths. Indeed, in their books there are many fabricated hadiths. Moreover, it is possible that the jahr with the basmala from the Prophet (peace be upon him) was on some occasions to demonstrate permissibility, or it was a teaching jahr, or it was incidental rather than intentional. And according to Abu Dawud in the book 'Al-Marasil' from Sa'id ibn Jubayr who said: 'The Messenger of Allah used to recite Bismillah aloud, and the people of Makkah used to call Musaylimah 'Al-Rahman', so they said: Muhammad calls to the one of Yamamah. So Allah commanded His Messenger to not recite them aloud until he died.' This indicates that the jahr was abrogated. If you desire complete detail on this research, refer to my treatise 'Ihkam al-Qantarah'.
Source pages p. 89

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute defending the Hanafi position that saying Bismillah aloud in prayer is not established from authentic hadith. The author begins by addressing the nomenclature of Surah Fatihah: calling it 'Surah Al-Hamd' is a later convention; the early practice of the Sahaba was to recite 'Al-Hamdu Lillahi Rabbil Alameen' without implying it is the surah's name. Then, a hadith attributed to Al-Awzai is examined: the version suggesting the Sahaba began with 'Umm al-Quran' is a narration by meaning, whereas the more authentic version (from Muslim's Sahih) shows they began with 'Al-Hamdu Lillahi Rabbil Alameen' without Bismillah. The author then refutes ahadith claiming the Prophet recited Bismillah aloud by demonstrating their chains contain unreliable narrators (liars, abandoned narrators). He further notes that these ahadith are only found in later collections that contain odd and fabricated material, not in the six canonical hadith books or major musnads. Finally, a hadith from Abu Dawud's Marasil is cited showing that jahr was abrogated because the Quraysh associated 'Rahman' with Musaylimah. The Hanafi position is thus proven: jahr with Bismillah is not part of the established Sunnah; rather, the basmala is recited silently according to the school.

Key Terms
الجهر بالبسملة (al-jahr bi al-basmala): Reciting the basmala (Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim) aloud during the prayer
الاستفتاح بأم القرآن (al-istiftah bi-umm al-quran): Opening the prayer with Surah Fatihah (Umm al-Quran)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi position on reciting Bismillah aloud in prayer according to this passage?
A) It is sunnah to recite it aloud.
B) It is prohibited to recite it aloud.
C) It is not established from authentic hadith; the practice of the Sahaba was to recite silently.
D) It is wajib to recite it aloud.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position that basmala is recited silently is based on the authentic practice of the Sahaba and the weakness of hadiths claiming jahr.
